Divine Transcendence

4 min
God's Transcendence Over Similarity and Opposites
Nasafi argues that affirming an opposite negates God's divinity and similarity negates His oneness, concluding with the Qur'anic verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why affirming any similarity or opposite to God negates His oneness and divinity, and how the Qur'an confirms His absolute transcendence.

Core Idea
To affirm an opposite or likeness for God is to deny His divinity and uniqueness.

This passage from Imam Nasafi's creed presents a fundamental argument for God's absolute transcendence. Before we can properly understand divine attributes, we must first clear our minds of any notion that God resembles creation or has an opposite. Nasafi shows that such ideas directly contradict the very meaning of divinity and oneness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic once to let its rhythm sink in, then read the English translation.
Notice the logical flow: if you affirm a partner, you deny His divinity; if you affirm similarity, you deny His oneness.
2
Identify the two key claims
The passage makes two interconnected arguments: (1) an opposite negates divinity, (2) similarity negates oneness. Underline these in the text.
These are the core of the argument.
3
Connect to the Qur'anic proof
Read the verse from Surah Ash-Shura and reflect on how it serves as the ultimate evidence for God's transcendence.
The verse is the 'tie-off' of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأجزاء - لزم القول بتعاليه عن الأشباه والأضداد، إذ في إثبات الضد نفي إلهيته، وفي التشابه نفي وحدانيته، إذ الخلق كلهم تحت اسم الأشكال والأضداد، وهما علما احتمال الفناء والعدم ونفي التوحيد عن الخلق.
والله تعالى واحد لا شبيه له دائم قائم لا ضد له ولاند، وهذا تأويل قوله تعالى:
﴿لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ﴾ [الشورى: ١١]... (۱)
And parts - it is necessary to affirm His transcendence over likenesses and opposites, for in affirming an opposite is a negation of His divinity, and in similarity is a negation of His oneness, for all creation are under the name of forms and opposites, and they are two signs of possibility of annihilation and non-existence and negation of monotheism from creation.
And Allah Almighty is One, without likeness, Eternal, Self-Subsisting, without opposite and without peer, and this is the interpretation of His saying, Exalted: "There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing" [Ash-Shura: 11]... (1)
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is an argument for God's absolute transcendence. The author states that if one affirms a partner or opposite for God, it necessarily negates His divinity (since a true god cannot have an equal) and his uniqueness (since similarity implies plurality). He explains that all created beings are characterized by forms and opposites, which are signs of their potential for annihilation and non-existence, and thus negate the pure monotheism that belongs only to the Creator. The passage culminates in the Qur'anic verse from Surah Ash-Shura, which is the definitive proof against any anthropomorphism or dualism.

Key Terms
أشباه
أضداد
وحدانية
إلهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is acceptable to speak of God having a 'peer' or 'opposite' as a metaphor.
Correction: This passage teaches that affirming any opposite or likeness for God directly negates His divinity and oneness, and is a violation of Tawhid.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do 'forms' (أشكال) and 'opposites' (أضداد) indicate about created beings?
A) They demonstrate God's power.
B) They are signs of potential annihilation and non-existence.
C) They prove that God has a form.
D) They show that God is similar to creation.

Key Takeaway
God's absolute transcendence means He has no likeness, no opposite, and no peer; any such attribution negates His divinity and oneness.

Refuting Anthropomorphism: Body and Form
Al-Lamishi refutes anthropomorphism by logical proof and citation of extreme views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Lamishi uses logical reasoning (no body → no form) and reports of extreme anthropomorphic claims to affirm God's transcendence.

Core Idea
God's transcendence precludes any form or composition.

Al-Lamishi, a classical Sunni theologian, addresses a dangerous misconception: that God might have a body or human form. He begins with a logical premise—if God is not a body, He cannot have a form, because form requires composition (tarkib). He then reports shocking anthropomorphic claims from extremist groups, showing how such beliefs implicitly attribute originatedness (huduth) to God. This passage is a powerful reminder of the Islamic commitment to tanzih (transcendence).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the logical flow from premise to conclusion.
The passage is a quote from al-Lamishi's 'al-Tamhid'.
2
Analyze the logical deduction
Identify the key logical step: if God is not described with a body (jism), then He cannot be described with a form (surah), because form cannot exist without composition (tarkib).
This is a core argument against anthropomorphism.
3
Examine the reported anthropomorphic claims
Note the four reported views: (1) God in human form with limbs, (2) as an old man with white beard, (3) as a beardless youth, (4) Hisham ibn al-Hakam's glistening ingot.
These are extreme examples meant to show the absurdity.
4
Understand the refutation
Al-Lamishi points out that all these descriptions imply huduth (originatedness). This is the decisive objection.
The passage ends with a declaration of negation by Allah's praise.
5
Reflect on common misunderstandings
Consider that denying a body does not deny all attributes—only bodily, composite attributes. God still has attributes like knowledge and power.
This avoids the opposite extreme of ta'til (stripping God of attributes).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وانظر إلى قول اللامشي في كتابه «التمهيد لقواعد التوحيد» متحدثًا عن نفي الجسم والصورة عن الله تعالى حيث قال ما صورته: «وإذا ثبت أن الله تعالى لا يوصف بالجسم، فلا يوصف بالصورة أيضًا؛ لأن الصورة لا وجود لها بدون التركيب. وقال بعض المجسمة ممن ذكرنا أساميهم إن الله تعالى على صورة الآدمي، وله من الأعضاء ما للآدمي، وإنه على صورة شيخ أبيض اللحية، وقال بعضهم: «إنه على صورة غلام أمرد له شعر جعد قطط». وحُكي عن هشام بن الحكم أنه قال: إنه كالسبيكة الصافية يتلألأ وفي كل ما قالوا إثبات كونه محدثًا. وقد نفينا ذلك بحمد الله تعالى»(۲).
And look at the saying of al-Lamishi in his book 'al-Tamhid li-Qawa'id al-Tawhid' speaking about negating body and form from Allah Almighty, where he said the following: 'And when it is established that Allah Almighty is not described with a body, then He is not described with a form either; because form has no existence without composition. And some of the anthropomorphists, whose names we have mentioned, said that Allah Almighty is in the form of a human, and He has the same limbs as a human, and that He is in the form of an old man with a white beard. And some of them said: "He is in the form of a beardless youth with curly hair." And it was narrated from Hisham ibn al-Hakam that he said: He is like a pure ingot that glistens. In all that they said, there is affirmation of His being originated. And we have denied that, by the praise of Allah Almighty' (2).
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a citation from al-Lamishi's work 'al-Tamhid' where he refutes anthropomorphism. He first establishes a logical point: if God is not a body, He cannot have a form, because form requires composition (tarkib). Then he reports the extreme claims of certain anthropomorphists: some said God is in the shape of a human with limbs, others described Him as an old man with a white beard, others as a beardless youth with curly hair, and Hisham ibn al-Hakam said He is like a pure glistening ingot. Al-Lamishi points out that all these descriptions imply originatedness (huduth), which is impossible for God. The passage ends by reaffirming the Sunni rejection of such views.

Key Terms
جسم
صورة
مجسمة
تركيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying a body means denying all attributes of God, including knowledge, power, etc.
Correction: The passage only denies bodily form and composition, not all attributes. God still has attributes like knowledge and power, but they are not like created attributes.

Checkpoint
According to al-Lamishi, why does denying a body lead to denying a form?
A) Because a body and form are the same.
B) Because form requires composition, and body is a prerequisite.
C) Because the Quran denies both.
D) Because the Prophet said so.

Key Takeaway
Al-Lamishi refutes anthropomorphism by showing that any form or body would imply composition and originatedness, which are impossible for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah, do you ever catch yourself forming a mental image? What does this lesson reveal about the danger of that habit, and what will you do this week to cleanse your heart from it?
?
How does the fact that any form implies originatedness change the way you approach descriptions of Allah in the Quran, such as 'the Most Merciful'? Are you willing to abandon every image you've ever held of Allah?
?
If someone told you that they feel closer to God by imagining Him as a light or a pure ingot, what would you say based on this lesson? What would you say to yourself if you secretly entertained such thoughts?

The Vision of Allah and Delight According to Disposition
Nasafi affirms the vision of Allah on Judgment Day and explains its delight according to worldly disposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the vision of Allah on Judgment Day is a real event whose delight varies according to each person's spiritual disposition in worldly life, and that true pleasure is in knowledge.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah is a delight shaped by your worldly heart.

This passage from Imam Nasafi's Bahr al-Kalam addresses one of the most profound topics of Islamic eschatology: the vision of Allah (ru'yat Allah) on the Day of Judgment. Nasafi affirms this vision while warning against those who deny it due to rationalistic limitations. He then explains that the joy of seeing Allah is not uniform—it corresponds to what dominated each person in this world, culminating in the recognition that true pleasure lies in knowledge. The passage ends with a heartfelt supplication for guidance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First read the Arabic passage or its literal translation to get the flow. Notice the warning against denial and the emphasis on personal disposition.
2
Identify the three key elements
Nasafi presents: (a) the reality of the vision, (b) the reason some deny it, (c) the proportional delight. How are they connected? Notice that 'the investigators confined pleasure to knowledge' is the key doctrinal point about true delight.
3
Reflect on the supplication
The passage ends with a personal plea for guidance. Consider why Nasafi includes this after the doctrinal statement.
This shows the practical application of the doctrine in the seeker's life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا وَرَدْنَا القِيَامَةَ وَتَجَلَّى لَنَا جَلَّ وَجْهُهُ بِمَا شَاءَ وَكَيْفَ شَاءَ، لَا تُنْكِرُهُ كَمَا يُنْكِرُهُ أَقْوَامٌ لِاحْتِجَابِهِمْ بِالتَّحَكُّمَاتِ العَقْلِيَّةِ وَغَلَبَةِ عَدَم التَّنْزِيهِ المُطْلَقِ عَلَى عُقُولِهِمْ، فَكَانُوا يُنْكِرُونَ رَبَّهُمْ جَلَّ أَمْرُهُ فِي الدُّنْيَا إِذَا تَعَرَّفَ لَهُمْ بِتَعَرُّفٍ جَلَالِيٍّ، أَوْ تَجَلَّى لَهُمْ بِمَا لَا يُلَائِمُ طِبَاعَهُمْ، فَيَظَلُّونَ فِي المُنَازَعَاتِ وَالرُّدُودِ وَالمُنَاقَضَاتِ مَعَ أَحْكَامِهِ .... فَإِنَّ كُلَّ رَاءٍ يَرَى رَبَّهُ جَلَّ عِزُّهُ يَوْمَ القِيَامَةِ يَلْتَذُّ بِرُؤْيَتِهِ حَسَبَ مَا كَانَ يَغْلِبُ عَلَيْهِ فِي الدُّنْيَا مِنْ ضُرُوبِ اللَّذَاذَاتِ وَغَلَبَاتِ المُشْتَهَيَاتِ، فَلِذَلِكَ حَصَرَ المُحَقِّقُونَ اللَّذَّةَ فِي المَعَارِفِ يَا كَرِيمُ. وَخُذْ إِلَيْكَ يَا اللهُ يَا اللهُ يَا اللهُ جَوْهَرَ عَقْلِي مِنْ بَيْنِ اشْتِبَاكِ الأَوْهَامِ وَتَضَادِّ الْأَفْكَارِ فِي كُلِّ نَازِلَةٍ إِلَى أَنْ تَهْدِيَهَا لِمَا اخْتَلَفُوا فِيهِ مِنَ الحَقِّ بِإِذْنِكَ، يَا هَادِي اهْدِنَا صِرَاطَكَ الْمُسْتَقِيمَ.
When we arrive at the Resurrection, and His majestic face manifests to us as He wills and how He wills, do not deny it as some people deny it due to their veiling by rational impositions and the predominance of the lack of absolute transcendence over their intellects, so they used to deny their Lord, majestic is His command, in this world when He made Himself known to them with a majestic self-disclosure, or manifested to them with what does not suit their natures, so they remain in disputes, rejections, and contradictions with His judgments.... For every seer who sees his Lord, majestic is His might, on the Day of Judgment delights in His vision according to what used to dominate him in this world from types of pleasures and overpowerings of desires. For that reason, the investigators have confined pleasure to knowledge, O Generous One. And take to Yourself, O Allah, O Allah, O Allah, the essence of my intellect from the entanglement of fancies and the contradiction of thoughts in every calamity, until You guide it to that concerning which they differed of the truth by Your permission, O Guide, guide us to Your straight path.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is an eschatological and spiritual reflection on the vision of Allah (ru'yat Allah) on the Day of Judgment. The author begins by affirming that when believers arrive at the Resurrection, Allah will manifest Himself to them in a manner and form He chooses. He then warns against denying this vision, as some groups do because they are veiled by rationalistic judgments and lack of true transcendence in their minds. These people denied their Lord even in this world when He revealed Himself in a majestic way or in ways not compatible with their natural inclinations, leading them into disputes and contradictions with divine decrees. The author then explains that every person who sees Allah on that Day will experience delight in the vision proportional to what dominated them in worldly life—whether pleasures or desires. For this reason, the true investigators (muhaqqiqun) restricted pleasure to knowledge (ma'arif), implying that the highest delight comes from cognizing God. The passage concludes with a heartfelt supplication asking Allah to protect the intellect from confusion and guide it to the truth amidst disagreements, seeking His straight path.

Key Terms
رؤية
تجلي
لذة
معارف
تحكمات عقلية
تنزيه مطلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The vision of Allah is a physical, sensory experience like seeing a physical object.
Correction: The passage explains that the delight of the vision is proportional to one's spiritual disposition and that true pleasure is in knowledge, indicating a cognitive rather than purely sensory experience.

Checkpoint
Why did the investigators (muhaqqiqun) confine pleasure to knowledge?
A) Because worldly pleasures are forbidden
B) Because knowledge is the only lasting delight in the afterlife
C) Because the highest delight of seeing Allah is a cognitive, not sensory, pleasure
D) Because they disliked sensual pleasures

Key Takeaway
The vision of Allah is real, and its delight depends on one's spiritual state in this world, culminating in the realization that true pleasure is in knowing Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that some people denied their Lord's majestic self-disclosure because it did not suit their natures, ask yourself: In what areas of your life do you still resist a truth from Allah because it clashes with your preferences? Are you willing to surrender that resistance today, or will it veil you from His vision on that Day?
?
The passage says your delight in seeing Allah will be according to what dominated you in this world—your pleasures and desires. What truly dominates your heart right now: the pursuit of fleeting gratifications or the longing to know your Lord? How is that choice shaping your eternal reward?
?
Nasafi concludes with a desperate plea for guidance amid confusion. Where in your own life are you still entangled in fancies and conflicting thoughts about the truth? Will you earnestly cry out to Allah to guide your intellect, or are you comfortable with the confusion? Do it now.

Divine Transcendence

God's Transcendence Over Space
Nasafi defines God's relation to space and istawa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi affirms God's transcendence over space, clarifying that His 'istawa' over the Throne does not imply physical location.

Core Idea
God is not in a place; He is the Creator of all places.

This lesson focuses on a central creedal point: God's relationship with space. Nasafi states that God created the Throne and time, and then 'established Himself over the Throne' (istawa). Immediately, he clarifies that this does not mean God sits or rests on the Throne, for the Throne is not a location for Him. Rather, God is the Creator of the Throne and of all locations, and He is above every place in a non-spatial sense of supremacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the sequence: creation of time and Throne, then istawa, then the negative statements.
The passage uses a very precise theological vocabulary.
2
Identify key terms
Find the words: العرش (Throne), المكان (place), الاستواء (establishing). Note how they are used in the context of God.
The term istawa is often misunderstood.
3
Analyse the doctrine
Understand the positive and negative statements: God is مستعل (elevated) but not the Throne; the Throne is not a resting place; God is the Creator of the Throne and place.
This is a classic formulation of tanzih (transcendence).
4
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: Why is it necessary to affirm that God is above every place without being spatial? What does this tell us about His nature?
This protects against anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَبْلَ أَنْ يَخْلُقَ الْوَقْتَ وَالزَّمَانَ ثُمَّ إِنَّهُ خَلَقَ الْوَقْتَ وَالْعَرْشَ وَاسْتَوَى عَلَى الْعَرْشِ وَهُوَ مُسْتَعْلٍ غَيْرُ الْعَرْشِ وَلَيْسَ الْعَرْشُ بِمُسْتَقَرٍّ لَهُ وَلَا مَكَانٌ بَلْ هُوَ خَالِقُ الْعَرْشِ وَالْمَكَانِ وَهُوَ أَعْظَمُ مِنْ أَنْ يُشْبَهَ بِالْمَكَانِ وَهُوَ فَوْقَ كُلِّ مَكَانٍ عَلِمَ مَا يَكُونُ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَكُونَ وَمَا لَا يَكُونُ إِذْ لَوْ كَانَ كَيْفَ يَكُونُ قَدْ سَبَقَ عِلْمُهُ فِي الْأَشْيَاءِ قَبْلَ كَوْنِهَا وَلَا يَكُونُ فِي مُلْكِهِ شَيْءٌ إِلَّا يَعْلَمُهُ وَمَشِيئَتُهُ وَتَقْدِيرُهُ وَقَضَاؤُهُ وَهُوَ كَمَا وَصَفَ نَفْسَهُ فِي كِتَابِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ صُورَةٍ وَكَمَا عَرَّفَ نَفْسَهُ مِنْ غَيْرِ رُؤْيَةٍ وَإِحَاطَةٍ فَقَالَ جَلَّ جَلَالُهُ لِرَسُولِهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قُلْ هُوَ اللَّهُ أَحَدٌ إِلَى آخِرِ السُّورَةِ وَهُوَ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى الْمَوْجُودِ نَقْضٌ عَلَى الْمُعَطِّلَةِ
Before He created time and duration, then indeed He created time and the Throne and established Himself over the Throne, and He is elevated, not the Throne, and the Throne is not a resting place for Him, nor a location, but He is the Creator of the Throne and the location, and He is greater than to be resembled to location, and He is above every place. He knows what will be before it is, and what will not be, if it were to be, how it would be. His knowledge preceded concerning things before their existence, and there is not in His dominion anything except that He knows it, and His will, decree, and ordainment. And He is as He described Himself in His Book without form, and as He defined Himself without vision and encompassing. So He, majestic is His glory, said to His Messenger, may God bless him and grant him peace: 'Say, He is God, the One,' to the end of the surah. And it is an indication to the Existent, a refutation against the Mu'attila (those who deny attributes).
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a theological statement that establishes God's absolute transcendence over space and time, while also refuting the Mu'attila (those who deny God's attributes). It begins by stating that God created time and the Throne, and then 'established Himself over the Throne' (istawa), immediately clarifying that He is not the Throne nor does the Throne serve as a location for Him. On the contrary, He is the Creator of the Throne and of space itself, and is utterly incomparable to spatial concepts. The phrase 'He is above every place' does not mean physical elevation but a status of supremacy. The passage then turns to God's knowledge: He knows all things, including what will not happen and how it would be if it did. His knowledge, will, decree, and ordainment encompass all. Finally, the author cites Surah al-Ikhlas (Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad) as the definitive scriptural proof that God's essence is unique and incomparable, serving as a refutation of the Mu'attila who strip God of His attributes. The mention of 'without form' and 'without vision and encompassing' underscores that God is not subject to human perception or comprehension.

Key Terms
العرش
المكان
الاستواء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God is physically located on the Throne.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that the Throne is not a resting place or location for God; He is the Creator of the Throne and space.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the correct understanding of 'istawa ala al-arsh'?
A) God sits on the Throne.
B) God is elevated but the Throne is not a location for Him.
C) God is inside the Throne.
D) The Throne contains God.

Key Takeaway
God is not spatially located; He is the Creator of all places and transcends them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly worship a God who is beyond all places, or do you unconsciously imagine Him in a specific direction? How would your prayer change if you internalized that He is not 'up there' but beyond all space?
?
What does it mean for your daily life that God does not 'move' or 'settle'? How can you find peace knowing that His attributes never change, even when your circumstances do?
?
The passage says God is 'greater than to be resembled to location.' Are there any subtle ways you have reduced God to something manageable or familiar? What would it cost you to let go of that mental image and submit to His absolute transcendence?

Divine Transcendence
beginner
5 min
God's Knowledge and the Refutation of the Mu'attila
Nasafi describes God's knowledge and will, then uses Surah al-Ikhlas to refute Mu'attila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi links God's comprehensive knowledge and will to Surah al-Ikhlas as a refutation of those who deny His attributes (Mu'attila).

Core Idea
God's knowledge and will encompass all, and His uniqueness is affirmed by the Qur'an.

Having established God's transcendence over space, Nasafi now turns to God's attributes of knowledge and will. He asserts that God knows all things before they exist, including what will not be. This is followed by a citation of Surah al-Ikhlas, which defines God's absolute oneness and serves as a decisive refutation of the Mu'attila, who strip God of His attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the flow: from knowledge of future events to the citation of Surah al-Ikhlas.
The passage ends with a strong statement of refutation.
2
Analyse the attributes mentioned
Identify the attributes: knowledge (علم), will (مشيئة), decree (تقدير), ordainment (قضاء). Understand their scope.
All these attributes are eternal and encompass all creation.
3
Understand the refutation
The passage says Surah al-Ikhlas is 'an indication to the Existent, a refutation against the Mu'attila.' Why is this specific surah used?
Surah al-Ikhlas emphasizes absolute oneness and incomparability.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider: How does affirming God's attributes refute the Mu'attila? What is the danger of denying attributes?
Denying attributes can lead to a concept of God that is empty or different from Islamic revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَبْلَ أَنْ يَخْلُقَ الْوَقْتَ وَالزَّمَانَ ثُمَّ إِنَّهُ خَلَقَ الْوَقْتَ وَالْعَرْشَ وَاسْتَوَى عَلَى الْعَرْشِ وَهُوَ مُسْتَعْلٍ غَيْرُ الْعَرْشِ وَلَيْسَ الْعَرْشُ بِمُسْتَقَرٍّ لَهُ وَلَا مَكَانٌ بَلْ هُوَ خَالِقُ الْعَرْشِ وَالْمَكَانِ وَهُوَ أَعْظَمُ مِنْ أَنْ يُشْبَهَ بِالْمَكَانِ وَهُوَ فَوْقَ كُلِّ مَكَانٍ عَلِمَ مَا يَكُونُ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَكُونَ وَمَا لَا يَكُونُ إِذْ لَوْ كَانَ كَيْفَ يَكُونُ قَدْ سَبَقَ عِلْمُهُ فِي الْأَشْيَاءِ قَبْلَ كَوْنِهَا وَلَا يَكُونُ فِي مُلْكِهِ شَيْءٌ إِلَّا يَعْلَمُهُ وَمَشِيئَتُهُ وَتَقْدِيرُهُ وَقَضَاؤُهُ وَهُوَ كَمَا وَصَفَ نَفْسَهُ فِي كِتَابِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ صُورَةٍ وَكَمَا عَرَّفَ نَفْسَهُ مِنْ غَيْرِ رُؤْيَةٍ وَإِحَاطَةٍ فَقَالَ جَلَّ جَلَالُهُ لِرَسُولِهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قُلْ هُوَ اللَّهُ أَحَدٌ إِلَى آخِرِ السُّورَةِ وَهُوَ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى الْمَوْجُودِ نَقْضٌ عَلَى الْمُعَطِّلَةِ
Before He created time and duration, then indeed He created time and the Throne and established Himself over the Throne, and He is elevated, not the Throne, and the Throne is not a resting place for Him, nor a location, but He is the Creator of the Throne and the location, and He is greater than to be resembled to location, and He is above every place. He knows what will be before it is, and what will not be, if it were to be, how it would be. His knowledge preceded concerning things before their existence, and there is not in His dominion anything except that He knows it, and His will, decree, and ordainment. And He is as He described Himself in His Book without form, and as He defined Himself without vision and encompassing. So He, majestic is His glory, said to His Messenger, may God bless him and grant him peace: 'Say, He is God, the One,' to the end of the surah. And it is an indication to the Existent, a refutation against the Mu'attila (those who deny attributes).
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a theological statement that establishes God's absolute transcendence over space and time, while also refuting the Mu'attila (those who deny God's attributes). It begins by stating that God created time and the Throne, and then 'established Himself over the Throne' (istawa), immediately clarifying that He is not the Throne nor does the Throne serve as a location for Him. On the contrary, He is the Creator of the Throne and of space itself, and is utterly incomparable to spatial concepts. The phrase 'He is above every place' does not mean physical elevation but a status of supremacy. The passage then turns to God's knowledge: He knows all things, including what will not happen and how it would be if it did. His knowledge, will, decree, and ordainment encompass all. Finally, the author cites Surah al-Ikhlas (Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad) as the definitive scriptural proof that God's essence is unique and incomparable, serving as a refutation of the Mu'attila who strip God of His attributes. The mention of 'without form' and 'without vision and encompassing' underscores that God is not subject to human perception or comprehension.

C) To describe God's form.

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge and will encompass all, and Surah al-Ikhlas powerfully refutes those who deny His attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The Mu'attila denied God's attributes out of a desire to protect His transcendence. But you may deny His attributes in practice by acting as if He does not see, know, or will what happens in your life. Where have you been living as though God is distant or indifferent? What one step will you take tonight to restore His rightful place in that area?

Ahl al-Sunna's Stance on Stars and Astrology
Nasafi states the Ahl al-Sunna view on stars and answers an objection about astrology in Idris's time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna position that celestial bodies are subservient to Allah with no independent management, and how the tradition answers the objection about astrology in the time of the prophets.

Core Idea
Stars have no management; all affairs are managed by Allah alone.

This lesson presents the Sunni creed regarding celestial bodies and addresses a historical challenge: if astrology was valid in the time of Prophet Idris, why is it prohibited today? The answer clarifies the nature of that knowledge and its abrogation, reinforcing the principle of tawheed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Notice the two-part structure: a creedal statement followed by an objection-and-answer.
The Arabic is partially corrupted; focus on the main ideas.
2
Identify the two main parts
Locate the creedal stance (stars are musakhkharat) and the objection about Idris and Ibrahim. Understand how the objection is framed.
3
Analyze the answer
The answer distinguishes between management (tadbir) by stars and Allah's direct teaching. Note how Ibrahim's knowledge is attributed to Allah's informing, not astrology.
The abrogation (naskh) in Sulayman's time is key.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why this distinction matters for tawheed and how it refutes astrological causation while accounting for prophetic examples.
Compare with common misunderstandings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال عامة أهل السنة والجماعة: هذه البروج والنجوم والشمس والقمر والنيرات مسخرات بأمر الله، ليس لها من التدبير شيء، ومدير الأمور هو الله تعالى. فإن قيل: علم النجوم كان حقاً في زمن إدريس عليه السلام، ومن قال بأنه نسخ فعليه الدليل. يدل عليه قوله تعالى: {فنظر نظرة في النجوم فقال إني سقيم} استدل بالنظر إلى النجوم. والجواب: قلنا: إن إبراهيم عليه السلام علم أنه يموت و[؟] في زمن إدريس عليه السلام. قلنا: ليس التدبير بالنجوم، ولكن الله تعالى أخبرهم في كتابهم أن نجم كذا إذا بلغ موضع كذا فاعلم أنه سيكون كذا وكذا، فعرفوا ذلك بتعريف الله تعالى إياه، ثم نسخ من وقت سليمان عليه السلام.
And the generality of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'ah said: These constellations, stars, sun, moon, and luminous bodies are subservient by the command of Allah; they have nothing of management, and the Manager of affairs is Allah Most High. For if it is said: The knowledge of the stars was true in the time of Idris, peace be upon him, and whoever says that it was abrogated must provide proof. Evidence for it is His statement Most High: {Then he cast a glance at the stars and said, 'Indeed, I am sick.'} He used the looking at the stars as evidence. And the answer: We say: Indeed, Ibrahim, peace be upon him, knew that he would die and [؟] in the time of Idris, peace be upon him. We say: There is no management by the stars, but Allah Most High informed them in their book that such a star, when it reaches such a place, know that such and such will happen. So they knew that by Allah's informing them, then it was abrogated from the time of Sulayman, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents the position of Ahl al-Sunna regarding celestial bodies and then addresses a critical objection concerning the legitimacy of astrology (ilm al-nujūm) in the time of the prophets. The passage begins by stating the creedal stance: all celestial bodies—constellations, stars, sun, moon, and other luminous objects—are maqad (subservient) by Allah's command. They have no independent power to manage or influence events; all affairs are managed by Allah alone. This refutes any notion of their having divine or causal efficacy.

The objection is then raised: it is claimed that astrology was valid and true in the time of Prophet Idris (Enoch). The objector demands proof from anyone who claims that this was later abrogated (naskh). The objector cites the Quranic verse about Prophet Ibrahim (Abraham): {Then he cast a glance at the stars and said, 'Indeed, I am sick.'} The objector interprets Ibrahim's looking at the stars as a proof that he used astrological observation, implying the legitimacy of such knowledge.

The answer (jawāb) is twofold. First, regarding Ibrahim: the author clarifies that Ibrahim knew he would die (or become sick) in the time of Idris—possibly linking to knowledge of his own lifespan—but the text here is corrupted and unclear. The main answer is that there is no concept of management (tadbīr) by the stars. Rather, Allah granted some prophets knowledge of future events by informing them directly. For example, Allah told them in a revealed book that when a particular star reaches a certain position, such-and-such event would occur. This knowledge came from Allah's teaching (ta’rīf), not from the intrinsic power of the stars. Later, at the time of Prophet Sulayman (Solomon), this specific knowledge was abrogated (naskh), meaning it was no longer lawful or valid to seek such knowledge from the stars. This answer upholds the principle of tawakkul and refutes any form of astrological causation, while accounting for historical instances of pre-Islamic prophetic knowledge that appear to involve stars.

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة
مسخرات
التدبير
علم النجوم
إدريس عليه السلام
نسخ
إبراهيم عليه السلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That stars or planets have independent power over events, or that the prophets' use of stars implies approval of astrology as a valid science.
Correction: The passage clarifies that stars are subservient and have no management; any prophetic knowledge involving stars came from Allah's direct teaching, not from the stars' intrinsic power, and this practice was later abrogated.

Checkpoint
What is the answer given regarding the story of Prophet Ibrahim looking at the stars?
A) He used astrology to predict his illness.
B) He knew he would die from that illness, and it was not by astrology but by Allah's informing.
C) The stars caused his sickness.
D) The questioner is mistaken; Prophet Ibrahim never looked at the stars.

Key Takeaway
The Ahl al-Sunna position is that stars are signs, not causes; any prophetic knowledge involving stars came from Allah's direct teaching, not from the stars themselves, and this was later abrogated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Do you ever catch yourself attributing life events—good or bad—to the position of planets, your zodiac sign, or coincidences, rather than submitting fully to Allah's sole management? What concrete action will you take this week to train your heart to rely only on Allah, even in small matters?
?
When you hear someone say 'It's written in the stars,' do you passively accept it or actively reject it as contrary to the Ahl al-Sunna stance? How will you change your own speech to reflect that Allah alone is the Manager of all affairs?
?

Are you seeking guidance from horoscopes, astrology apps, or superstitious signs instead of turning directly to the Quran and Allah? Refutation of Astrological Causation
Nasafi refutes astrology: stars do not cause events; they are signs taught by God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Islamic theology denies that stars cause events and affirms that all knowledge comes from God alone.

Core Idea
Stars are signs, not causes; all true knowledge comes from God's teaching.

Imam Nasafi presents a concise refutation of astrological causation. He explains that people who knew about stars' indications only knew because God informed them in His Book. This lesson examines his argument and the abrogation of such knowledge from the time of Prophet Solomon.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own wording guide your understanding.
The Arabic is from a heavily corrupted manuscript; rely on the translation for clarity.
2
Identify the core refutation
The passage opens with 'قلنا ليس التدبير بالنجوم' (We say: the arrangement is not by the stars). This is a direct denial that stars control events.
The word 'tadbīr' implies governance or management.
3
Understand the source of knowledge
Nasafi explains that any knowledge of events linked to stars came only because God informed people in His Book (taʻrīf Allāh). The stars themselves are not sources of knowledge.
This affirms that all true knowledge is from divine revelation.
4
Reflect on the abrogation
The passage mentions that this type of knowledge was abrogated (naskh) from the time of Solomon. Consider why a previously valid means might be cancelled.
Abrogation shows that even permitted means are subject to divine will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلنا ليس التدبير بالنجوم ولكن الله تعالى أخبرهم في كتابهم أن نجم كذا إذا بلغ موضع كذا فاعلم أنه سيكون كذا وكذا فعرفوا ذلك بتعريف الله تعالى إياه ثم نسخ من وقت سليمان على السلام حين غابت الشمس بعد ما دخل الليل عليهم ذلك الحساب والله الهادي.
We say: the arrangement (al-tadbīr) is not by the stars, but rather God Almighty informed them in His Book that such-and-such a star, when it reaches such-and-such a position, then know that such-and-such will happen. So they knew that by God Almighty's definition (taʻrīf) of it to them. Then it was abrogated (nuskha) from the time of Solomon, peace be upon him, when the sun set after the night had entered upon them — that reckoning. And God is the Guide.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of astrology — the belief that stars cause or determine events. The author begins by stating 'We say' (a direct refutation), asserting that the arrangement or governance of affairs (al-tadbīr) is not by the stars. Instead, God Almighty informed people in His Book (likely referring to prophets or previous scriptures) that when a certain star reaches a certain position, it indicates that something will happen. Their knowledge, therefore, came from God's informing (taʻrīf), not from the stars themselves. The author then mentions that this knowledge was abrogated (nuskha) from the time of Prophet Solomon (peace be upon him), specifically referencing an event where the sun set after night had entered upon them, marking a change in the reckoning. The passage concludes with 'And God is the Guide' (al-Hādī), affirming that guidance comes only from God.

Key Terms
التدبير بالنجوم (tadbīr bi-l-nujūm)
تعريف الله (taʻrīf Allāh)
نسخ (naskh)
سليمان (Sulaymān)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Stars inherently indicate future events or cause them.
Correction: Any knowledge of events via stars comes only from God's teaching, not from the stars themselves, and such knowledge can be abrogated by divine will.

Checkpoint

A) By the natural properties of the star
B) By God's informing (taʻrīf) through His Book
C) By astrological calculations handed down from Solomon
D) By the star's position in the sky

Key Takeaway
Islamic theology strictly denies that stars have causal power; all true knowledge and guidance come from Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Opening Creed: God's Transcendence and Knowledge
Author opens with praise and states core beliefs about God's attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Imam Nasafi, God is transcendent, free from form and place, and His knowledge encompasses all things before they exist.

Core Idea
God is not confined to any place or form; His knowledge is eternal.

Imam Nasafi opens his creed with praise of Allah and immediately establishes key principles of Islamic theology. In these few lines, he affirms God's absolute transcendence beyond physical attributes and locations, and declares that God's knowledge precedes all creation. This sets the foundation for the entire work.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the opening praise formula and the declarations about God.
The text is from an old manuscript and contains some uncertain readings.
2
Identify the affirmations
List the divine attributes mentioned: majesty, honor, no form, no image, above all places, all-encompassing knowledge.
These are core Ash'ari/Maturidi beliefs.
3
Reflect on the Throne
The passage explicitly states the Throne is not a resting place for God. Why is this important?
This refutes anthropomorphism.

الحمد لله ذي الجلال والاكرام والصلاء الأنام علي الرواحنا الكرام [؟] اعلم اني اعتقد [؟] ولا شكل له ولا صيادله [؟] وليس العرش له مستقر [؟] بل هو فوق كل مكان [؟] يعلم ما يكون قبل ان يكون [؟] وزلزلة الساعة شي وما مكون من أواخر الموجودات [؟] يعلم ما كان من المخلوقات.
Praise be to Allah, Possessor of Majesty and Honor, and prayers upon the people? [؟] upon our noble souls? [؟]. Know that I believe [؟] and He has no form nor image [؟] and the Throne is not a resting place for Him [؟] rather He is above every place [؟] He knows what will be before it is [؟] and the earthquake of the Hour is a thing and what is composed of the last of existents [؟] He knows what was of the creatures.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the book, combining praise of Allah with a concise theological confession. It opens with the standard formula of praise (الحمد لله ذي الجلال والاكرام) and prayers. The author then declares his belief, though the exact wording is obscured by poor OCR. Key affirmations include God's transcendence: He has no shape (لا شكل له) and no image (لا صيادله, likely a corruption of لا صورة له). The Throne (العرش) is not a place of settlement for Him, emphasizing that He is above all places. Furthermore, God's knowledge is eternal and all-encompassing: He knows what will be before it exists, including the Hour and all created things. This sets the tone for a work grounded in Ash'ari or Maturidi kalam, focusing on tanzih (divine transcendence) and God's attributes.

The Sunni Refutation of Astrological Claims
Nasafi states the Sunni view that celestial bodies are subservient and refutes astrological claims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that celestial bodies are subservient and have no administrative power, and how a Qur'anic verse supports this.

Core Idea
Celestial bodies serve, not rule — only Allah administers all affairs.

This lesson presents a foundational Sunni doctrine that directly refutes astrological claims. Imam Nasafi states the position of Ahl al-Sunna wal-Jama'a that the stars, sun, moon, and all celestial entities are subservient to Allah's command and have no independent power. A Qur'anic proof is provided to anchor this belief in divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the strong contrast between 'musakhkharat' (subservient) and 'tadbir' (administration).
The word 'musakhkharat' implies they are harnessed for a purpose, not autonomous.
2
Understand the doctrinal claim
Identify the two parts: (1) celestial bodies are subservient and have no administrative power, (2) Allah alone is the Administrator.
3
Examine the Qur'anic proof
Look at the verse from Surah Al-Kahf. Why does Nasafi use this particular verse? It shows celestial bodies were not witnesses to creation, so they cannot have power over it.
This verse is often used to refute shirk, but here it is specifically applied to astrological claims.
4
Reflect on the refutation
Consider how this doctrine counters astrology: if stars have no power, they cannot influence events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: النجوم والشمس والقمر وجميع الغيرات مسخرات ليس لها من التدبير شيء، ومدبر الأمور هو الله تعالى. والدليل على ذلك قوله تعالى: (ما أشهدتهم خلق السموات والأرض ولا خلق أنفسهم).
And Ahl al-Sunna wal-Jama'a said: The stars, the sun, the moon, and all the celestial bodies are subservient; they have no power of administration. The Administrator of affairs is Allah Almighty. The evidence for that is His statement: 'I did not call them to witness the creation of the heavens and the earth, nor the creation of themselves.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a statement of the Sunni doctrine regarding celestial bodies. It asserts that they are subservient (musakhkharat) and lack independent administrative power (tadbir). All affairs are administered by Allah alone. The proof is the Qur'anic verse from Surah Al-Kahf (18:51), which indicates that these bodies were not witnesses to creation, thus they have no power or knowledge of such matters. This refutes astrological claims that stars influence events.

Key Terms
مسخرات
تدبير
مدبر

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse simply refutes shirk in general, not specifically astrological claims.
Correction: Nasafi uses it specifically to deny celestial bodies any role in creation or administration, which directly refutes astrology.

Checkpoint

A) They have independent power over events
B) They are subservient and have no administrative power
C) They control human destiny
D) They are divine

Key Takeaway
Sunni doctrine rejects any independent influence of celestial bodies, affirming that only Allah administers all affairs.

?

Stars Are Subservient, Not Managers
Nasafi states the Ahl al-Sunnah position that stars have no independent power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni theological position that celestial bodies have no independent power or management over worldly events.

Core Idea
Stars and planets are subservient tools, not independent managers.

This passage from Imam Nasafi's 'Bahr al-Kalam' presents a fundamental creedal point: the stars, sun, moon, and all planets are created entities subjected to Allah's command. They possess no inherent power to influence events. This teaching directly refutes astrological claims of celestial influence and affirms that all management belongs solely to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic text and its English translation. Note that the passage is concise, making a clear statement of belief.
The Quranic quote is partially corrupted in the source; focus on the creedal assertion.
2
Identify the key terms
Notice the terms 'Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah', 'musakhkharat', 'tadbir', and 'mudabbir al-umur'. These are key theological concepts.
'Musakhkharat' means subservient or subjected, implying total control by Allah.
3
Understand the negation of management
The phrase 'ليس لها من التدبير شيء' explicitly denies any management role to celestial bodies. Ask yourself: why is this important?
This guards against shirk (associating partners with Allah) in the form of believing in astrological influences.
4
Reflect on the Quranic support
Even though the verse is incomplete, the author cites the Quran to support the doctrine. Reflect on how the Quran describes celestial bodies as subservient.
Common verses include 'والشمس والقمر بحسبان' (The sun and the moon follow a reckoning) or 'وسخر لكم الشمس والقمر' (And He subjected for you the sun and the moon).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: [؟] النجوم والشمس والقمر وجميع الكواكب مسخرات ليس لها من التدبير شيء، ومدبر الأمور هو الله تعالى كما قال تعالى: {والشمس والقمر [؟]} [؟]
And Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah said: [؟] the stars, the sun, and the moon, and all the planets are subservient, they have nothing of management, and the Manager of affairs is Allah the Exalted, as He said the Exalted: {And the sun and the moon [؟]} [؟]
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage presents the orthodox Sunni position regarding celestial bodies. It begins by attributing the view to Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, establishing that the stars, sun, moon, and all planets are 'musakhkharat' (subservient or subjected) – meaning they are under God's command and have no independent will or power. The phrase 'ليس لها من التدبير شيء' explicitly denies them any role in the management or governance of worldly affairs. All management (tadbir) belongs solely to Allah. The author then supports this with a partial Qur'anic citation, likely referring to verses like 'والشمس والقمر بحسبان' or 'والشمس والقمر والنجوم مسخرات بأمره'. The argument refutes astrological claims that celestial bodies influence events directly.

Correction: The passage clarifies that they are subservient (musakhkharat) and have no management whatsoever. All affairs are managed solely by Allah.

Key Takeaway

?

God's Oneness and Eternal Attributes
Nasafi affirms God's oneness and eternal attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni creed regarding God's absolute oneness, individuality, and eternal description with attributes.

Core Idea
God is One, Individual, Eternal, described by His attributes without change.

Imam Nasafi begins his creed by affirming the foundational beliefs about God's essence. He declares that God is One (wahid), Individual (fard), and Eternal (qadim), without any partner or likeness. This lesson explores these core assertions and their implications for Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic text and translation
Read the passage from 'اعلموا أني أعتقد' to 'أبداً موصوفاً بصفاته' and the corresponding translation. Notice the direct and assertive tone.
The passage is a direct statement of personal belief (i'tiqad).
2
Identify the key terms
Look for the terms: واحد, فرد, قديم, لا شريك, لا مثل, لا شكل, لا حد, لا تعديل. Understand their meanings in this context.
These negations guard against any form of association or limitation.
3
Understand the eternity of attributes
The phrase 'لم يزل... ولا يزال...' emphasizes that God has always been and always will be described by His attributes. Reflect on why this is important for avoiding change in God.
Attributes like knowledge and power are not acquired but are eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلموا أني أعتقد أن الله واحد فرد قديم [أزلي] وأنه لا شريك له ولا [مثيل] ولا [شكل] ولا [حد] ولا [تعديل] لم يزل واحداً فرداً [أحداً] ولا يزال كذلك أبداً [موصوفاً] بصفاته المنزه عن النقصان العالم [الغني] [بلا شريك] كان قبل أن يخلق المكان وقبل أن يخلق الوقت والزمان ثم إنه خلق الوقت والعرش واستوى على العرش [استواء] [يليق به] وليس [فوق كل مكان] [على] [ما يكون قبل أن يكون] [وما لا يكون إن لو كان كيف يكون قد سبق علمه] [بكل شيء] [وقدره] وقضائه [نافذ] [وكما عرف نفسه] [من غير صورة]
Know that I believe that God is One, Individual, Eternal, and that He has no partner, nor likeness, nor form, nor limit, nor change. He has not ceased to be One, Individual, and does not cease to be thus forever, described by His attributes, transcendent above deficiency, the Knower, the Self-Sufficient, without partner. He was before He created space and before He created time and duration. Then He created time and the Throne, and He 'istawa' (established Himself) upon the Throne in a manner befitting Him. And He is not above every place, [He knows] what was before it existed and what does not exist, if it were to exist how it would be. His knowledge preceded everything, and His decree and predestination are effective. And as He knew Himself, without form.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a creedal declaration (i'tiqad) by Imam Nasafi, setting forth foundational Sunni beliefs about God's essence and attributes. The author begins by affirming that God is one (wahid), individual (fard), and eternal (qadim), with no partners, likeness, form, limit, or change in His essence. He emphasizes that God has always been and always will be described by His attributes, which are free from any deficiency. The author then states that God existed before the creation of space (makan) and time (waqt wa zaman), establishing His absolute priority. He then affirms that God created time and the Throne, and He established Himself over the Throne (istawa) in a manner befitting His majesty—an important Ash'ari position that avoids anthropomorphism. The phrase 'and He is not above every place' likely means He is not confined to a spatial location, though He is 'above' in a transcendental sense. The passage continues by asserting God's comprehensive knowledge of all things, including what was and what would be, and the effectiveness of His decree and predestination. Finally, it states that God knows Himself without form, rejecting any corporeal representation. The overall passage provides a concise summary of God's oneness, eternity, and transcendence, guarding against anthropomorphism (tashbih) and negation of attributes (ta'til).

Key Terms
واحد
فرد
قديم
لا شريك
لا شكل
لا حد
صفاته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's attributes are created or change over time.
Correction: The creed affirms that God has always been described by His attributes and never ceases to be so; His attributes are eternal and unchanging.

Checkpoint
According to the creed, how long has God been described by His attributes?
A) From the beginning of creation
B) Since time began
C) He has always been described by them
D) Only after He created the universe

Key Takeaway
God is eternally one and forever described by His attributes without any partner or change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you declare that God is 'واحد' and 'فرد', does your heart truly abandon any reliance on created beings, or do you still seek security in people, status, or possessions? What would it cost you to live as if only God is truly One and sufficient?
?
The passage affirms that God is described by His attributes eternally—‘لم يزل ولا يزال موصوفاً بصفاته’. Do you treat God’s attributes (like His mercy, power, knowledge) as unchanging realities, or do you sometimes doubt them when life is hard? How would your daily prayers change if you were absolutely certain that God’s mercy never wavers?
?
God has no ‘شكل’ (form) and no ‘حد’ (limit)—yet you often imagine Him in your mind. What mental image of God do you need to repent of? Will you actively remind yourself that He is beyond any form, even as you pray?

God's Transcendence and the Istiwa'
Nasafi discusses God's priority over creation and the manner of His istiwa'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni theology affirms God's transcendence above space and time and interprets the istiwa' (establishing upon the Throne) in a manner befitting His majesty.

Core Idea
God is beyond space and time; His istiwa' is without modality.

After affirming God's essence and attributes, Imam Nasafi turns to God's relation to creation. He states that God existed before space and time, and then He created them. The controversial verse about God's istiwa' over the Throne is addressed with the principle of 'without form or modality', which is a hallmark of Ash'ari theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on transcendence
Read the Arabic from 'المنزه عن النقصان' to 'وليس فوق كل مكان' and the translation. Note the sequence: transcendence, then priority over space/time, then istiwa'.
The term 'المنزه' (transcendent) sets the tone.
2
Understand God's priority over creation
The phrase 'كان قبل أن يخلق المكان وقبل أن يخلق الوقت والزمان' establishes that God is not dependent on space or time; they are His creations.
This refutes the idea that God is located in space.
3
Analyze the istiwa' statement
The creed says 'استوى على العرش استواءً يليق به'—He established Himself without modality. Compare this to literal interpretations.
Ash'ari theology rejects physical contact or location.
4
Reflect on the negation of spatial confinement
The clause 'وليس فوق كل مكان' (He is not above every place) is puzzling; it likely means He is not spatially located anywhere, even above.
Some interpret this as denying that He is confined to a location above.

God's Knowledge, Decree, and Self-Knowledge
Nasafi affirms God's comprehensive knowledge and effective decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni belief that God's knowledge encompasses all things, His decree is effective, and He knows Himself without form.

Core Idea
God's knowledge is eternal and all-encompassing; His decree is decisive; He is beyond any form.

The final part of Nasafi's creed delves into God's attributes of knowledge and will. It affirms that God knew everything before it existed, that His decree is inescapable, and that His self-knowledge is without any form or representation. This lesson explores these profound doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on knowledge and decree
Read the Arabic from 'قد سبق علمه' to 'من غير صورة' and the translation. Notice how it connects knowledge, decree, and self-knowledge.
The passage is brief but dense.
2
Understand the scope of divine knowledge
The phrase 'قد سبق علمه بكل شيء' (His knowledge preceded everything) asserts that God knows all past, present, and future, as well as possibilities.
The clause about 'ما لا يكون لو كان كيف يكون' shows knowledge of hypotheticals.
3
Reflect on the effectiveness of decree
The term 'قضائه نافذ' (His decree is effective) means God's will is irresistible and nothing happens contrary to His decree.
This is a key Ash'ari doctrine of divine predestination.
4
Contemplate God's self-knowledge without form
The final phrase 'وكما عرف نفسه من غير صورة' indicates that God's knowledge of Himself is not through any image or form, rejecting anthropomorphism.
This complements the earlier negation of form (لا شكل).

The Stars Are in the Lowest Heaven
Nasafi contrasts astrologers' view with Ahl al-Sunnah and cites Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic theological position on the location of the stars and the Quranic evidence used to support it.

Core Idea
Stars are in the lowest heaven, not independent sources of power.

Imam Nasafi presents a key theological disagreement: do the stars reside in the fourth heaven, as astrologers claim, or in the lowest heaven, as Ahl al-Sunnah affirm? In this lesson, we will examine the two views and the Quranic proof texts that settle the matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two opposing views.
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that there are two distinct opinions: the astrologers' claim and the Ahl al-Sunnah's position.
The astrologers are referred to as 'ahl al-nujūm', and the opposing group as 'ahl al-sunnah wa ahl al-tafsīr'.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence provided.
Two Quranic verses are cited: Q. 67:5 (adornment of the lowest heaven with lamps) and Q. 18:86 (the sun setting in a muddy spring). Consider how each verse supports the claim that stars are in the lowest heaven.
The word 'maṣābīḥ' (lamps) in 67:5 is understood as stars.
3
Reflect on the theological significance.
Why does it matter whether stars are in the fourth or lowest heaven? This distinction refutes astrological claims of stellar autonomy and reinforces Islamic tawheed—all created things are subservient to Allah.
The placement of stars in the nearest heaven emphasizes their role as signs, not causes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال اهل النجوم الشمس والقرو النجوم في السماء الرابعة وقال اهل انتة والم الصحة والتفسير في السماء الدنيا يدل عليه قوله تعالى تازينا السماء الدنيا بنتة الكواكب قورتی انا زينا السماء الدنيا بمصابيح وكذلك قو در تعالي في قصر في القرنين منی او رایج مغروب الشمس ابد تا تغريب في عين حماية و جولا مبلغ اور تمام
The astrologers said: the sun, moon, and stars are in the fourth heaven. And the people of correctness and interpretation said: they are in the lowest heaven. That is indicated by His statement, the Exalted: 'We have adorned the lowest heaven with lamps' [67:5], and likewise His statement, the Exalted, in the story of Dhul-Qarnayn: 'until when he reached the setting of the sun, he found it setting in a muddy spring' [18:86].
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage records a disagreement about the location of the stars. The astrologers (ahl al-nujūm) claimed the sun, moon, and stars are in the fourth heaven, implying a higher status and perhaps influence. The opposing view, attributed to 'ahl al-sunnah wa ahl al-tafsīr' (the people of the sunnah and interpretation), insists they are in the lowest heaven (al-samā' al-dunyā). The proof is drawn from two Quranic verses: first, Q. 67:5, which explicitly states that the lowest heaven is adorned with 'lamps' (maṣābīḥ), referring to stars. Second, Q. 18:86, which describes the sun setting in a muddy spring, indicating its proximity to the earth. The point is to show that stars are not autonomous entities with independent power but are subservient signs placed in the nearest heaven, thus refuting astrological claims of influence.

Key Terms
نجوم
السماء الدنيا
مصابيح
مسخرات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Stars have independent influence over events on earth.
Correction: The Quran places them in the lowest heaven as subservient lamps, denying any autonomy and affirming that all power belongs to Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the Ahl al-Sunnah and Ahl al-Tafsir as presented here, where are the stars located?
A) In the fourth heaven
B) In the lowest heaven
C) On earth
D) In the seventh heaven

Key Takeaway
The stars are located in the lowest heaven as subordinate signs of Allah's power, refuting astrological claims of autonomy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the night sky, do you see humble lamps adorning Allah's lowest heaven, or do you still feel a pull to attribute power to the stars? How can you train your heart to see only His majesty in their subordination?
?
Have you ever consulted horoscopes or felt influenced by zodiac signs? Knowing that these stars are merely close objects in the lowest heaven, what steps will you take to place your trust solely in Allah?
?
If the sun, which is so mighty, sets in a muddy spring by Allah's command, what does that reveal about your own perceived power? In what area of your life do you need to submit to the reality that you are not independent but entirely dependent on the Creator?

Allah's Absolute Uniqueness and Attributes
Nasafi declares God's incomparability and mentions His attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah is absolutely unique and transcendent, with no likeness or peer, and that He possesses perfect attributes such as knowledge and power.

Core Idea
Allah has no likeness or peer; He is unique in essence and attributes.

Imam Nasafi begins by commanding the reader to 'know'—this is not mere information but a foundational creedal affirmation. He declares that Allah has no likeness (mithl) and no peer (shibh), establishing tanzih (divine transcendence). He then mentions two attributes: Allah is the Knower of the unseen and the Holder of the Throne, affirming His omniscience and absolute sovereignty.

Guided Path
1
Read the declaration of transcendence
Read the Arabic passage slowly. Notice the commanding tone 'اعلموا' (Know). Focus on the two negations: 'no likeness' and 'no peer'.
These two phrases are the bedrock of tanzih.
2
Understand the meaning of 'no likeness and no peer'
Reflect on why these negations are essential. Allah is unlike anything we can imagine. He has no equal or rival. This refutes anthropomorphism and shirk.
The attributes that follow are not comparable to creation.
3
Reflect on the attributes mentioned
Consider what it means that Allah is 'the Knower of the unseen' and 'the Holder of the Throne'. These affirm His perfect knowledge and absolute power.
Life and peace are also mentioned, but the text is unclear.

Commentary
This passage is a declaration of divine transcendence (tanzih). The author begins by commanding the reader to know that Allah has no likeness (mithl) and no peer (shibh). Due to severe OCR corruption, the remainder of the passage is unclear, but it appears to continue listing attributes such as 'life' (al-hayah) and 'peace' (al-salam). The author's intent is to establish the core Quranic and creedal understanding of God's uniqueness and perfection.

Refuting Anthropomorphic Interpretations of Divine Attributes
Nasafi refutes literal interpretations of divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical Sunni scholars interpret anthropomorphic verses and hadith metaphorically to preserve God's transcendence (tanzih).

Core Idea
God's attributes are beyond human likeness; apparent anthropomorphisms are metaphors for His power and actions.

This passage from Imam Nasafi addresses several objections raised by anthropomorphists who take Quranic verses and hadith literally. He refutes each interpretation by providing a metaphorical meaning that upholds God's transcendence. The focus is on terms like 'grip', 'leg', 'fingers', and 'foot'. Let's examine his arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how Nasafi presents objections before refuting them.
2
Identify the four objections
The passage addresses four anthropomorphic claims: grip (qabdah), leg (saq), two fingers (isba'ayn), and foot (qadam). Find each one in the text.
Each objection is followed by a refutation.
3
Study the refutations
For each objection, note the metaphorical interpretation Nasafi offers. Understand how he reinterprets the literal meaning to preserve tanzih.
For example, 'grip' means dominion, 'leg' means a great matter, etc.
4
Understand the final principle
Nasafi concludes by negating attributes like coming and going from God, and cites Prophet Ibrahim's argument against a moving deity.
This reinforces the core idea of divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعالى والارض جميعًا قبضته يوم القيامة والسموات مطويات بيمينه والجواب عن قول قبضة يوم القيامة يعني في ملكه وقدرته كما يقال هذه الأرض في قبضتي وملكي وهم احتجوا باثبات الساق الله تعالى لقوله يوم يكشف عن ساق وفي الخبر ان قلوب العباد بين اصبعين الرحمن يقلبها كيف يشاء وفي الخبر ان جهنم تقول هل من مزيد فيضع الرب قدم فيها فتقول قط قط يعني حسبي حسبي قلنا أراد بالساق امر عظيم صعبا وقال بعضهم اراد به ساق جهنم لما روي في الخبر ان لجهنم ثلاثين الف كأس في كل رأس ثلاثون الف قم فكذلك يكون ان يكون له ساق ومعنى الخبر قلوب العباد بين اصبعين الرحمن اراد به الاثر ذكره الأصمعي واراد به الاثر وهو [؟] ماهر اللغة وقوله حجة معناه بين الاثرين من اثار الرحمن وهو التوفيق والخذلان فمن وفقه الله تعالى يشتغل بالطاعة ومن خذله يشتغل بالمعصية ومعنى الخبر يضع الجبار قدم فيها بكسر القاف وهو الصحيح من الروايات معناه من كان في قدر علمه من الكفار والله الهادي [؟] ولا يجوز ان يوصف الله تعالى بالمجيء والذهاب لأن المجيء والذهاب من صفات المخلوقين وإمارات المحدثين وهما صفتان منفيتان عن الله تعالى الأخرى ان ابراهيم صلوات الله عليه كيف استدل بالمنتقل من مكان الى مكان أنه ليس برب لما قال فلما اقل قال لا احب الافلين
He says: The earth entirely will be [within] His grip on the Day of Resurrection, and the heavens will be folded in His right hand. And the answer to the saying 'a handful on the Day of Resurrection' is that it means in His dominion and power, just as it is said 'this land is in my grip and possession'. And they argued by affirming the leg for God Almighty because of His saying 'on the Day when the leg will be uncovered'. And in the hadith: 'Verily the hearts of the servants are between two fingers of the Most Merciful, He turns them as He wills'. And in the hadith: 'Verily Hell says: Is there any more? So the Lord places His foot in it, and it says: Enough, enough, meaning sufficient for me'. We said: By 'leg' He meant a great, difficult matter. And some said He meant the leg of Hell, because it was narrated in the hadith that Hell has thirty thousand goblets, in every head thirty thousand [things], so it is possible that it has a leg. And the meaning of the hadith 'the hearts of the servants are between two fingers of the Most Merciful' – He intended by it 'the effect'. Al-Asma'i mentioned it, and he intended by it the effect, and he is a master of language, and his saying is an argument. Its meaning is between two effects from the effects of the Most Merciful, which are success and abandonment. So whoever God grants success occupies himself with obedience, and whoever He abandons occupies himself with disobedience. And the meaning of the hadith 'the Compeller places His foot in it' – with kasrah on the qaf, and that is the correct narration – its meaning is: whoever is in the extent of His knowledge of the disbelievers, and God is the Guide. It is not permissible to describe God Almighty with coming and going, because coming and going are attributes of created beings and marks of originated things, and they are two attributes negated from God Almighty. The other [point] is that Ibrahim, peace be upon him, how did he infer from the moving from one place to another that He is not a Lord? When he said: 'When it set, he said: I do not like those that set'.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage addresses several objections raised by those who interpret anthropomorphic verses and hadith literally. The author presents each objection and then refutes it by providing a metaphorical interpretation that upholds God's transcendence. First, regarding the verse 'the earth entirely will be within His grip' (39:67), he explains that 'grip' means dominion and power, not a physical hand. Then, the objection about 'leg' (saq) from the verse 'on the Day when the leg will be uncovered' (68:42) is answered by interpreting 'leg' as a great, difficult matter, or alternatively as the leg of Hell (a creature). Next, the hadith about the hearts between two fingers is explained as referring to two effects (athar) of God: success (tawfiq) and abandonment (khidhlan). Finally, the hadith about the 'foot' (qadam) is interpreted as referring to those disbelievers who are within God's knowledge. The author concludes by affirming that coming and going cannot be attributed to God, as they are characteristics of created beings. He then references the example of Prophet Ibrahim (as) who, by observing the setting of celestial bodies, concluded that a true Lord cannot be subject to movement or change.

قبضة (qabdah)
ساق (saq)
اصبعين (isba'ayn)
قدم (qadam)
توفيق (tawfiq)
خذلان (khidhlan)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some mistakenly think that these verses and hadith attribute bodily parts to God literally.
Correction: The passage clarifies that they must be understood metaphorically to preserve tanzih.

Checkpoint

A) A physical hand holding the earth
B) God's dominion and power
C) A specific location
D) A metaphorical punishment

Key Takeaway
Anthropomorphic expressions in revelation are to be interpreted metaphorically to protect God's transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses like 'the hand of God is above their hands,' does your heart truly affirm that God has no limb, or does a mental image still creep in? What will you do to purify your understanding of Allah?
?
The hadith about hearts between 'two fingers' teaches that your obedience depends on God's success (tawfiq) and your sin on His abandonment (khidhlan). Do you live each moment conscious that your actions are only possible by His will? What one change will you make today to rely more on Him?
?
Prophet Ibrahim rejected a god that moves (sets). Are there any thoughts or ideas you hold about Allah that imply change, limitation, or similarity to creation? How will you actively replace them with the correct tawhid belief?

Allah's Transcendence of Space and the Throne
Nasafi affirms istawa and Allah's transcendence of space.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's istawa over the Throne does not imply spatial location, and that Allah is transcendent above all creation, including space and the Throne.

Core Idea
Allah is above every place, not as a location, but as the Creator and Holder of space.

This lesson examines a key passage from Imam Nasafi’s work on the divine attributes. It addresses the Qur'anic verse of istawa (establishing over the Throne) while firmly guarding Allah’s transcendence. The passage clarifies that Allah is independent of the Throne and that the Throne is not a location for Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully, noticing the sequence of statements. Pay attention to the conjunctions 'then', 'and', 'rather'.
The passage begins with 'thumma' indicating sequence.
2
Identify the key affirmations and negations
Note what the passage affirms about Allah (He created the Throne, istawa, is independent, is the Holder) and what it negates (Throne is not a resting place or location).
This distinction is crucial for avoiding anthropomorphism.
3
Reflect on the meaning of 'fawqa kulli makan'
Consider why the author ends with 'above every place'. This is not a spatial statement but a declaration of transcendence.
The common misunderstanding is to take this literally as a place.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنه تعالى خلق العرش والوقت، واستوى على العرش، وهو مستغن عن العرش، وليس العرش له بمستقر ولا بمكان، بل هو مُمسك العرش والمكان، وهو أعظم من أن يسعه المكان، وهو فوق كلّ مكان.
Then He Most High created the Throne and time, and He established Himself over the Throne, and He is independent of the Throne, and the Throne is not for Him a resting place nor a location. Rather, He is the Holder of the Throne and space, and He is greater than that space should contain Him, and He is above every place.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage addresses the Qur'anic verse of istawa (establishing over the Throne). Imam Nasafi affirms that Allah created the Throne and time, then He 'istawa' over the Throne. However, he immediately safeguards transcendence: Allah is mustaghni (independent) of the Throne. The Throne is not a mustaqarr (settling place) nor a makan (location) for Him. Instead, Allah is the one who holds and sustains the Throne and space itself. The phrase 'fawqa kulli makan' (above every place) is not a spatial location but a statement of His highness and transcendence. This is standard Sunni tafwid (consigning the modality to Allah) while affirming the attribute without tashbih (anthropomorphism).

Key Terms
العرش
استوى
مستقر
مكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Interpreting 'fawqa kulli makan' as a physical location in space.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Allah is not contained by space; He is the Creator and Holder of space, so 'above every place' means transcendence, not spatial location.

Checkpoint

B) Allah is independent of the Throne and the Throne is not a location for Him
C) The Throne is a part of Allah
D) Allah rests on the Throne

Key Takeaway
Allah's istawa over the Throne does not imply spatial location; He is transcendent and independent of all creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The passage says Allah holds the Throne and space—He is the Holder, not the held. Are there areas of your life where you feel insecure, as if your 'place' is unstable? How does the truth that the Creator of all places holds you affect your fear of losing your footing?
?
The Throne is the greatest creation, yet Allah is independent of it. What created thing—status, wealth, relationships—do you sometimes rely on as if it were your 'throne'? Will you consciously evaluate your attachments today and realign your dependence on Allah alone?

God's Independence from Space and Istiwa'
Nasafi explains creation of Throne, time, and God's istiwa' without spatial dependence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi affirms the Quranic istiwa' while denying any spatial dependence for Allah, thereby preserving divine transcendence.

Core Idea
God is above every place, not contained by any place.

This passage from Nasafi's creed tackles a crucial point of Islamic theology: how to understand the Quranic statement that Allah 'established Himself over the Throne' without falling into anthropomorphism. Nasafi immediately clarifies that the Throne is not a resting place or location for Allah—He is independent of it and holds all space. Let's read the source to see how he balances affirmation and negation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the sequence: creation, istiwa', then clarifications.
2
Identify affirmations and negations
List what Nasafi affirms about Allah (e.g., created the Throne, established Himself) and what he negates (e.g., need for the Throne, being contained by place).
The negations are crucial for tanzih (transcendence).
3
Reflect on the theological purpose
Ask yourself: How does this passage protect Allah from anthropomorphism while accepting the Qur'anic text?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنه تعالى خلق العرش والوقت، واستوى على العرش، وهو مستغن عن العرش، وليس العرش له بمستقر ولا بمكان، بل هو مُمسك العرش والمكان، وهو أعظم من أن يسعه المكان، وهو فوق كلّ مكان.

Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a theological explanation of God's relation to the Throne and space. It begins by stating that God created the Throne (al-‘arsh) and time (al-waqt). Then it affirms that He 'established Himself over the Throne' (istawā ‘alā al-‘arsh), a phrase from the Quran (20:5). However, immediately it clarifies that God is independent (mustaghnī) of the Throne—He does not need it. The Throne is neither a resting place (mustaqarr) nor a place (makān) for Him. Instead, God is the holder of both the Throne and place (mumsik al-‘arsh wa al-makān); He sustains them. The passage then negates any spatial limitation: God is greater than that place should contain Him, and He is above every place. This defends divine transcendence against anthropomorphism (tashbīh).

Divine Transcendence
beginner
