Refutation of Anthropomorphism and Interpretation of the Seeing Hadith
Nasafi refutes anthropomorphism and interprets a hadith about seeing Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi rejects literal interpretation of the hadith 'I saw my Lord' and how he defends divine transcendence.

Core Idea
Allah is beyond form; seeing is not literal.

The hadith of the Prophet's ascension includes a report that he saw his Lord in a beautiful form. Some have taken this literally, implying Allah has a form. Nasafi refutes this by offering alternative interpretations that preserve divine transcendence. This passage shows the careful method of Ahl al-Sunna in handling ambiguous texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation. Notice how Nasafi moves from a general principle to a specific hadith interpretation.
The passage begins with a strong statement about combining Creator and created.
2
Understand the objection
Identify the objection: the hadith seems to say the Prophet saw Allah in a form. Why would this be problematic?
This objection is the basis for anthropomorphism.
3
Examine the two interpretations
Nasafi gives two possible meanings: either the Prophet saw Jibril, or he himself was in a beautiful form. Consider how each preserves Allah's transcendence.
The word 'Lord' can be used honorifically for a master.
4
Connect to the Quranic verse
Notice how Surah al-Hashr 59:24 is used as evidence. Reflect on its implications for divine attributes.
Reading 'al-musawwir' in the accusative would attribute form to Allah, which is disbelief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا قلتم بأن بعض أجزائه إله، وبعض أجزائه ليس بإله، يكون هذا جمعا بين الخالق والمخلوق [ والرازق والمرزوق ] ومن قال هذا يكفر. فإن قيل: ما رُوي عن النبي لا أنه قال: رأيت ربي ليلة المعراج في أحسن صورة فقال : يا محمد فيمَ يختصم الملأ الأعلى فقلت: لا أدري. قلنا: معنى الخبر رأيت ربي في أحسن صورة يعني سيدي جبرائيل عليه السلام في أحسن صورة. وقال بعضهم: رأيت ربي في أحسن صورة يعني: رأيتُ وكنتُ في أحسن صورة، يدل على صحة ما قلنا قوله تعالى: ﴿هُوَ اللَّهُ الْخَالِقُ الْبَارِئُ الْمُصَوِّرُ ﴾ [الحشر: ٢٤] وإن قرأ (المصوّر) بالنصب عمداً يكفر، وإن أخطأ تفسد صلاته.
And if you say that some of its parts are God, and some of its parts are not God, this combines the Creator and the created [and the Provider and the provided-for], and whoever says this disbelieves. If it is said: What is reported from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'I saw my Lord on the night of the Ascension in the most beautiful form, and He said: O Muhammad, about what does the most high assembly dispute? And I said: I do not know.' We say: The meaning of the report is 'I saw my Lord in the most beautiful form' meaning I saw my master Jibril (peace be upon him) in the most beautiful form. And some said: 'I saw my Lord in the most beautiful form' means: I saw and I was in the most beautiful form. Supporting what we have said is the statement of Allah Most High: 'He is Allah, the Creator, the Originator, the Bestower of forms' [Quran 59:24]. And if someone reads 'al-musawwir' in the accusative intentionally, he disbelieves, and if he errs, his prayer is invalid.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of anthropomorphism. It first dismisses the idea that any part of creation could be divine, stating that this would mix Creator and created and constitutes disbelief. Then it addresses an objection based on a hadith where the Prophet reportedly saw his Lord. The author offers two interpretations: either the Prophet saw Jibril in a beautiful form, or the phrase means the Prophet himself was in a beautiful form. The Quranic verse from Surah al-Hashr is cited to show that Allah is the Bestower of forms, not someone who has a form. Finally, a warning is given about misreading the verse: reading 'al-musawwir' in the accusative intentionally is disbelief, while a mistake only invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms

مخلوق
رازق
مرزوق
صورة
جبرائيل
معراج
مصوّر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet saw Allah in a physical form during the Mi'raj.
Correction: The hadith is interpreted figuratively; 'Lord' refers to Jibril or the Prophet's own state, and Allah is described as the Bestower of forms, not having a form.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what does the Prophet's statement 'I saw my Lord in the most beautiful form' mean?
A) He saw Allah in a physical form.
B) He saw Jibril in a beautiful form.
C) He saw his own reflection.
D) He was speaking metaphorically.

Key Takeaway
The hadith of seeing the Lord on the night of Mi'raj does not imply Allah has a form; it is interpreted as seeing Jibril or the Prophet's own state.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever visualized Allah in your mind, even in a vague or metaphorical way? How does Nasafi's insistence that Allah is al-Musawwir (the Bestower of forms) and therefore formless challenge that tendency in you? What will you do to actively train your heart to think of Allah beyond any form?
?
If someone you respect told you the hadith 'I saw my Lord in the most beautiful form' proves Allah has a body, would you have the courage to explain the interpretation? What would prevent you from speaking up, and how can you prepare yourself now to defend tanzih with knowledge and humility?
?
The Prophet himself said 'I do not know' when asked about the heavenly dispute. Does your own certainty about what you know of Allah ever become a barrier to admitting ignorance? When will you next sit in humility before the Quran, letting it shape your understanding rather than your preconceptions?

Refuting the Karramiyya: Istiwa Means Domination
Nasafi refutes the Karramiyya claim using linguistic evidence that istiwa means istawla.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi refutes the Karramiyya's anthropomorphic interpretation of Allah's istiwa using linguistic evidence.

Core Idea
Istiwa means domination, not physical settlement — language proves divine transcendence.

The Karramiyya sect claimed that Allah literally settled on the Throne, citing the Quranic verse 'al-Rahman 'ala al-arsh istawa.' Imam Nasafi refutes this by showing that the word 'istawa' in Arabic can mean 'dominated' (istawla), not necessarily physical contact. He supports this with a Persian gloss and classical poetry. This lesson explores how linguistic argument defends Allah's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Karramiyya claim
Read the passage to see what the Karramiyya said and how they used the Quranic verse as proof.
Notice they claimed Allah filled the Throne.
2
Examine the linguistic refutation
Nasafi presents three pieces of evidence: the opinion of some exegetes, a Persian gloss, and a line of poetry. Each shows 'istawa' can mean domination.
The poetry example is key: Bishr became 'mustawin' over Iraq without war, meaning he dominated it.
3
Apply the lesson to divine transcendence
Reflect on why this refutation matters: it preserves Allah's transcendence and rejects anthropomorphism.
This is a standard method in kalam to defend tanzih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في بيان معنى الاستواء على العرش ]
قالت الكرَّامية : إن الله تعالى استقرَّ على العرش حتى امتلأ منه حجتهم قوله تعالى: ﴿الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ﴾ [طه: ٥].
است (۱)
قلنا لهم: قال بعض أهل التفسير : يعني استولى قيل : بالفارسية: بر عرش پادشاه
يدل عليه قول القائل:
قد استوى بشر على العِرَاقِ من غير سيف ودم مِهْرَاقِ
يعني: استولى.
Chapter: On explaining the meaning of istiwa (being established) upon the Throne. The Karramiyya said: Indeed Allah, exalted, settled upon the Throne until He filled it. Their proof is the saying of Allah, exalted: 'The Most Merciful is established (istawa) upon the Throne' [Ta-Ha: 5]. (1) We said to them: Some of the exegetes said: He means He dominated (istawla). It is said: in Persian: 'bar 'arsh padshah' (the King is upon the Throne). This is supported by the saying of the poet: 'Bishr became istawa over Iraq without sword or spilled blood' meaning: He dominated.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage defines the theological position of the Karramiyya sect regarding the meaning of Allah's istiwa upon the Throne. They claim that Allah literally settled and filled the Throne, citing the Quranic verse 'The Most Merciful is established upon the Throne.' Nasafi then presents a linguistic refutation: the word istiwa here means 'istawla' (domination or conquest), not physical settlement. He supports this with a Persian gloss and a line of Arabic poetry where 'istawa' is used in the sense of gaining control over a region without violence. The argument is that the context of the verse and linguistic usage prove that istiwa implies sovereign power, not spatial occupancy.

Key Terms
الكرَّامية
استوى
استولى
العرش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Karramiyya interpretation that Allah literally sits on the Throne is a valid understanding of the verse.
Correction: Linguistic analysis and classical usage show that 'istawa' in this context means 'dominated' (istawla), not physical settlement. Thus, the verse affirms Allah's sovereignty, not His physical location.

Checkpoint
What linguistic meaning of 'istawa' does Nasafi use to refute the Karramiyya?
A) settled
B) dominated
C) ascended
D) leaned

Key Takeaway
Nasafi uses linguistic evidence — exegesis, Persian gloss, and poetry — to show that 'istawa' in the verse means 'istawla' (domination), not physical settlement, thus preserving divine transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the verse 'ar-Rahmanu 'ala al-'arshi istawa,' do you catch yourself imagining a spatial location for Allah? How can you train your heart to instead feel His absolute sovereignty without confinement?
?
In your daily life, you rely on Allah's control over everything. How does understanding istiwa as domination deepen your trust that He is in charge of every affair, even when circumstances seem chaotic?
?
If you were to explain the meaning of istiwa to a child, would your explanation risk implying a physical attribute? How can this lesson purify your own mental image of Allah before you teach others?

Transmission by Meaning and the Slave Girl Hadith
Nasafi critiques the slave girl hadith as a case of distortion by transmission by meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the practice of narrating hadith by meaning can introduce distortions, using the slave girl hadith as a case study, and why the question 'Where is Allah?' is inconsistent with Islamic transcendence.

Core Idea
The slave girl hadith warns us not to take literally narrations that slipped through transmission by meaning.

Nasafi continues his discussion on the effects of riwaya bil-ma'na (transmission by meaning) on hadith. He now examines a well-known but problematic narration—the Prophet asking a slave girl 'Where is Allah?'—to show how even a famous story can be altered. This challenges those who use such hadith to claim Allah is spatially located.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to grasp Nasafi's argument. Notice his tone: he is correcting a misunderstanding.
The passage is a continuous reflection, not a list.
2
Identify the key claim
Nasafi affirms that transmission by meaning has affected many hadith, and the slave girl story is a prime example. Find where he states that the question 'Where is Allah?' appears only in one chain.
This is the core evidence for his argument.
3
Understand the theological point
Nasafi explains that Allah cannot be confined to a place; He is the Creator of space and time. This principle (tanzih) is violated by the question. Reflect on why this matters for tawhid.
The passage ends with a warning against anthropomorphism (tashbih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلت: وقد صدق الشيخ رحمه الله في قوله: «فعلِمَ أنه قد فعلت الرواية بالمعنى في الحديث ما فعلت» فمن المعلوم والمقرر أن جُلَّ السنة نقل بالمعنى، ومن هذا الباب حديث الجارية المشهور، فقد ورد في أحد طرقه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سألها «أين الله ؟ فأشارت إلى السماء؟» فهذا مما فعلت فيه الرواية بالمعنى ما فعلت أيضًا، لأن الرواية الأخرى لم يرد بها هذا السؤال الذي لم يرد عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في أي حديث آخر، حيث كان لا يقبل إسلام من يُسلم دون مثل هذه الأسئلة التي لا تتفق مع ما يليق بالله عزّ وجل، فالله تعالى لا أين له حتى يُسأل عنه بالأين ، فهو خالق المكان والزمان وهو على ما عليه كان لم يتغير ولم يتبدل سبحانه وتعالى عما يصفون، وقد غابت هذه القاعدة عن أذهان كثيرن ممن تورّطوا في التشبيه. والله أعلى وأعلم.
I say: The shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) spoke truth in his saying: 'So know that transmission by meaning has done to hadith what it has done.' It is known and established that most of the Sunnah was transmitted by meaning. From this category is the famous hadith of the slave girl, for it came in one of its chains that the Prophet (peace be upon him) asked her: 'Where is Allah?' and she pointed to the sky. This is from what transmission by meaning has done to it as well, because the other narration does not contain this question, which has not come from the Prophet (peace be upon him) in any other hadith, and he would not accept the Islam of one who converts without such questions that are inconsistent with what befits Allah, Almighty and Majestic. Allah, exalted, has no 'where' such that He is asked about location; He is the Creator of place and time, and He is as He ever was, unchanged and unaltered, exalted is He above what they describe. This principle has escaped the minds of many who have fallen into anthropomorphism. And Allah is most High and most Knowing.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a critical reflection on how the practice of narrating hadith by meaning (riwaya bil-ma'na) has introduced distortions. Nasafi endorses the shaykh's statement that this practice has affected hadith. He gives the example of the well-known hadith of the slave girl, where in one version the Prophet asks 'Where is Allah?' and she points to the sky. Nasafi points out that this version is not corroborated by other authentic chains; such a question does not appear elsewhere from the Prophet, and it would be inconsistent with Islamic teaching that Allah is not confined to a location. The correct understanding is that Allah is beyond space and time. This principle, known as tanzih (transcendence), is often forgotten by those who fall into anthropomorphism (tashbih). The passage serves as a warning against taking such narrations literally without considering the principles of tawhid.

Key Terms
الرواية بالمعنى
الجارية
أين
التشبيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some Muslims believe the slave girl hadith proves that Allah is literally in the sky, based on the wording 'Where is Allah?' and the pointing to the sky.
Correction: Nasafi shows that this version is a product of transmission by meaning, not a reliable proof for Allah's location. The correct belief is that Allah is transcendent, beyond space.

Checkpoint
Why does Nasafi consider the slave girl hadith as an example of distortion by transmission by meaning?
A) The hadith is weak in all chains
B) The question 'Where is Allah?' appears only in one version and not in other authentic narrations
C) The slave girl was not a reliable narrator
D) The hadith contradicts the Quran

Key Takeaway
Transmission by meaning can introduce words that contradict core Islamic beliefs, such as the transcendence of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a hadith that seems to describe Allah in human terms, do you immediately try to reconcile it with tawhid, or do you accept it literally? What does that reveal about the state of your heart regarding Allah's transcendence?
?
The scholars who transmitted by meaning had good intentions, yet errors still crept in. In your own understanding of Islam, where might you be relying on a 'transmitted meaning' that actually distorts the truth? What would it cost you to go back to the original sources?
?
Nasafi says that many have fallen into anthropomorphism by neglecting the principle that Allah has no 'where'. Is there any belief or practice you hold that—if honestly examined—implies a direction or place for Allah? Will you abandon it today, even if it feels uncomfortable?

The Argument from Allah's Pre-existence
Nasafi's first rational argument: pre-existence negates movement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why movement to the Throne is impossible for Allah because He existed before creation.

Core Idea
Allah's timeless existence rules out any physical movement.

Nasafi begins with a simple yet profound argument: Allah existed eternally before the Throne was created. To claim He then moved to it would attribute change and movement to Him, which are marks of created beings. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the first argument
Read the Arabic passage for the first argument carefully. Notice how Nasafi states the premise that Allah existed before the Throne.
This argument relies on God's eternal nature.
2
Identify the logical connection
Understand why pre-existence negates movement: moving implies change from one state to another, which is impossible for the eternal God.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Nasafi concludes that movement is a quality of created beings. See how this follows from the premise.
This establishes tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن الله تعالى كان قبل أن يخلق العرش فلا يجوز أن يقال: بأنه انتقل إلى العرش؛ لأن الانتقال من صفات المخلوقين وأمارات المحدثين والله تعالى منزّه عن ذلك، ولأن من قال بالاستقرار على العرش فلا يخلو إما أن يقول بأنه مثل العرش أو العرش أكبر منه، أو هو أكبر من العرش، وأياً ما كان فقائله كافر، لأنه جعله محدوداً.
And because Allah, exalted, existed before He created the Throne, so it is not permissible to say that He moved to the Throne; for movement is a quality of created beings and a sign of temporal things, and Allah, exalted, is transcendent from that. And because whoever says that He settled upon the Throne cannot avoid either saying that He is like the Throne, or the Throne is greater than Him, or He is greater than the Throne. Whichever it is, the speaker is a disbeliever (kafir), because he has made Him limited.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage presents two rational arguments against the belief that Allah literally settled on the Throne. First, since Allah existed eternally before creating the Throne, to say He then moved to it would imply change and movement, which are attributes of created, temporal beings. This contradicts Allah's transcendence (tanzih). Second, if one insists on literal settlement, it forces a dilemma: either Allah is comparable to the Throne in size, or the Throne is greater than Him, or He is greater than the Throne. All three options lead to limitation (tahdid), which is impossible for Allah. Therefore, anyone who holds such a view is considered a disbeliever (kafir). This argument relies on the impossibility of applying spatial dimensions to God.

Key Terms
الانتقال
المخلوقين
المحدثين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this argument denies the attribute of istiwa entirely.
Correction: It only rejects literal physical movement, not the Quranic affirmation of istiwa as a divine attribute beyond human comprehension.

Checkpoint
What is the main premise of Nasafi's first argument against literal settlement?
A) The Throne is too great for Allah
B) Allah existed before the Throne
C) The Throne was created after Allah
D) Movement is only for humans

Key Takeaway
Allah's existence before creation makes movement to the Throne impossible.

The Dilemma of Limitation
Nasafi's second rational argument: the three-option dilemma of limitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three impossible options that follow from claiming Allah settled on the Throne, and why each leads to disbelief.

Core Idea
Literal settlement forces a choice that leads to Allah's limitation and blasphemy.

Nasafi presents a devastating dilemma: if Allah settled on the Throne, He must either be like the Throne, smaller, or larger. All options imply limitation, which is impossible for the Creator. This lesson analyzes the three branches.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma passage
Read the Arabic text of the second argument. Notice the three options Nasafi enumerates.
2
Understand each option
Consider each possibility: Allah like the Throne, the Throne greater, or Allah greater. Reflect on why each necessitates limitation (tahdid).
Limitation means being confined to space, which is impossible for Allah.
3
Grasp the consequence
Nasafi declares that holding any of these options makes one a disbeliever (kafir). Understand why limitation contradicts divine perfection.
This argument concludes with a strong takfir for those who insist on literal settlement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن الله تعالى كان قبل أن يخلق العرش فلا يجوز أن يقال: بأنه انتقل إلى العرش؛ لأن الانتقال من صفات المخلوقين وأمارات المحدثين والله تعالى منزّه عن ذلك، ولأن من قال بالاستقرار على العرش فلا يخلو إما أن يقول بأنه مثل العرش أو العرش أكبر منه، أو هو أكبر من العرش، وأياً ما كان فقائله كافر، لأنه جعله محدوداً.

And because whoever says that He settled upon the Throne cannot avoid either saying that He is like the Throne, or the Throne is greater than Him, or He is greater than the Throne. Whichever it is, the speaker is a disbeliever (kafir), because he has made Him limited.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage presents two rational arguments against the belief that Allah literally settled on the Throne. First, since Allah existed eternally before creating the Throne, to say He then moved to it would imply change and movement, which are attributes of created, temporal beings. This contradicts Allah's transcendence (tanzih). Second, if one insists on literal settlement, it forces a dilemma: either Allah is comparable to the Throne in size, or the Throne is greater than Him, or He is greater than the Throne. All three options lead to limitation (tahdid), which is impossible for Allah. Therefore, anyone who holds such a view is considered a disbeliever (kafir). This argument relies on the impossibility of applying spatial dimensions to God.

Imam Malik on Istiwa: The Proper Attitude
Nasafi cites Malik's statement on istiwa and rebuke of Jahm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the attribute of istiwa: affirming its meaning while negating any modality (kayf), and recognizing that questioning the how is a sign of innovation.

Core Idea
Istiwa is known in meaning, unknown in how, and asking about it is innovation.

Imam Malik, the great scholar of Medina, succinctly defined the correct stance towards Allah's attribute of istiwa (establishing upon the throne). This passage, preserved by Nasafi, not only articulates the principle but also illustrates it through the famous incident of Jahm ibn Safwan. As you read, note how Malik distinguishes between affirming the meaning and refusing to delve into the how.

Guided Path
1
Read Malik's statement
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the four parts: istiwa not unknown, kayf not comprehensible, belief obligatory, asking bid'ah.
Malik's phrasing is concise and direct.
2
Understand the three principles
Identify that Malik affirms the meaning of istiwa (it is known), denies any modality (kayf is unknowable), and declares belief obligatory while inquiry into the how is innovation.
This is the classic Sunni approach to divine attributes.
3
Reflect on the Jahm incident
Consider why Malik reacted so strongly: the questioner asked about the 'how' of istiwa. Malik saw this as a heresy and ordered him slapped.
Jahm ibn Safwan was the founder of the Jahmi sect, which denied all divine attributes.
4
Connect to broader Aqeedah
Ask yourself: what does this teach about dealing with ambiguous verses? The Salaf affirmed the meaning but stopped short of asking how.
This principle applies to all attributes: tafwid of modality, not of meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن مالك بن أنس رضي الله عنه إمام أهل المدينة أنه قال: «الاستواء غير مجهول، والكيف غير معقول ، والإيمان به واجب، والسؤال عنه بدعة، وقال للسائل : ما أراك إلا ضالاً. وأمره بالصفع فإذا هو جهم بن صفوان عليه اللعنة».
And from Malik ibn Anas, may Allah be pleased with him, the imam of the people of Medina, that he said: 'Al-istiwa (establishing upon the throne) is not unknown, and the how (al-kayf) is not comprehensible, and belief in it is obligatory, and asking about it is innovation (bid'ah). And he said to the questioner: I see you only as misguided. And he ordered him to be slapped, and it turned out to be Jahm ibn Safwan, may curse be upon him.'
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a transmitted proof (naqli dalil) from Imam Malik, a leading authority of Ahl al-Sunnah. Nasafi cites it to establish the correct stance on the attribute of istiwa. The passage consists of three parts: 1) Malik's famous statement defining istiwa as known in meaning (ma'na) but unknown in modality (kayfiyya). He says al-istiwa is not unknown, meaning its lexical meaning (establishing, ascending) is known but the exact nature (kayf) is beyond human comprehension. 2) He then states the obligations: belief in it is wajib, and asking about its modality is bid'ah (religious innovation) because the Salaf did not inquire. 3) Finally, he relates an incident where a questioner asked about the kayf of istiwa; Malik recognized him as Jahm ibn Safwan, the founder of the Jahmi sect, and ordered that he be slapped for his heretical questioning. This shows that questioning the how of divine attributes is evidence of deviation.

Key Terms
الاستواء
الكيف
بدعة
جهم بن صفوان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Salaf did not interpret istiwa at all, leaving it completely ambiguous.
Correction: Malik affirms the meaning of istiwa ('it is not unknown'), so the Salaf did have a lexical understanding. The unknown part is the kayf (modality), not the meaning.

Checkpoint

B) Obligatory
C) Innovation (bid'ah)

Key Takeaway
Affirming the attribute of istiwa while denying any modality is a core Sunni position, and questioning the how is a sign of deviation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Rational Refutation of Allah's Settlement on the Throne
Nasafi uses rational argument to refute settlement on the Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the rational argument shows that Allah's settlement on the Throne is impossible and that any spatial relation implies limitation.

Core Idea
Allah's transcendence precludes any spatial change or limitation.

This passage from Imam Nasafi presents a rational argument that refutes anthropomorphic interpretations of Allah's relation to the Throne. It is not enough to simply reject such ideas; we must reason why they are impossible. Here, Nasafi provides two clear rational proofs that establish divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the literal translation. Let the argument flow naturally before analyzing.
Pay attention to the logical connectors 'because' and 'and because'.
2
Identify the two arguments
The passage contains two main arguments: first, the argument from pre-existence that refutes transfer; second, the trichotomy argument about size that refutes settlement.
Notice that the second argument has three possible cases.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why each argument leads to the conclusion that any notion of settlement or transfer is kufr. What does this teach us about Allah's transcendence?
Think about the concept of 'limitedness' (mahdud).
4
Connect to broader theology
Relate this argument to the proper understanding of ayat al-istiwa (the verse about Allah's establishment over the Throne) without anthropomorphism.
This argument protects tawhid and divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأن الله تعالى كان قبل أن يخلق العرش فلا يجوز أن يقال: بأنه انتقل إلى العرش؛ لأن الانتقال من صفات المخلوقين وأمارات المحدثين والله تعالى منزّه عن ذلك، ولأن من قال بالاستقرار على العرش فلا يخلو إما أن يقول بأنه مثل العرش أو العرش أكبر منه، أو هو أكبر من العرش، وأياً ما كان فقائله كافر، لأنه جعله محدوداً.
And because Allah, exalted, existed before creating the Throne, it is not permissible to say that He transferred to the Throne; because transferring (al-intiqal) is among the attributes of created beings and signs of contingent things, and Allah, exalted, is transcendent above that. And because whoever says that He settled (al-istiqrar) upon the Throne, then it is inevitable that he says either that He is like the Throne, or the Throne is greater than Him, or He is greater than the Throne. And whichever it may be, its speaker is a disbeliever because he has made Him limited.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof (aqli dalil) against the anthropomorphic notion that Allah physically settled on the Throne. The argument proceeds in two steps: First, Nasafi states the premise that Allah existed before the Throne was created. If one claims that Allah later 'transferred' to the Throne, that would imply change and movement, which are attributes of created beings (makhluqin) and contingent beings (muhdathin). Allah is transcendently above such change. Second, Nasafi refutes the claim of 'settling' (istiqrar) by analyzing three possible interpretations: 1) the being settling could be equal to the Throne in size, 2) the Throne could be larger, or 3) the being could be larger than the Throne. All three entail that Allah is limited (mahdud) and comparable to His creation, which is kufr (disbelief). Thus, the only correct position is to affirm istiwa without kayf and without ta'til.

Key Terms
الانتقال
المخلوقين
المحدثين
الاستقرار
محدود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that Allah's settlement on the Throne does not imply equivalence or limitation, and that it is permissible without specifying how.
Correction: This argument shows that any notion of spatial relation to the Throne inevitably leads to one of the three possibilities, all of which imply limitation and are thus kufr.

Checkpoint

D) The Prophet forbade it

Key Takeaway
The rational proof shows that any spatial attribute ascribed to Allah inevitably leads to limitation and is therefore disbelief.

The argument says that any spatial relation implies limitation. Ali's Teaching on Allah's Eternality Without Place
Nasafi cites Ali's response to the question of Allah's location before creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the question 'Where was Allah before creation?' is invalid and how Ali's response establishes Allah's transcendence of place and time.

Core Idea
Allah existed without place or time and remains unchanged.

This short but powerful narration from Ali ibn Abi Talib cuts through a common misconception. When asked about Allah's location before the Throne, Ali does not point to a place. Instead, he exposes the flaw in the question itself, affirming that Allah's existence is beyond spatial and temporal dimensions. This lesson unpacks the theological depth of his brief answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a question, then Ali's response. Pay attention to the key terms: مكان (place), زمان (time), أين (where).
2
Analyze Ali's reframing of the question
Ali points out that 'where' (أين) presupposes place (مكان). By doing so, he shows the question is invalid when applied to Allah before creation, as place did not exist.
3
Understand the principle of divine immutability
Ali's statement 'He is now as He was' teaches that Allah does not change. After creating place and time, Allah does not acquire a location. He remains transcendent.
This refutes the anthropomorphic idea that Allah 'settles' on the Throne after creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن علي رضي الله عنه أنه سُئل: أين كان ربنا قبل أن خلق العرش ؟ فقال رضي الله عنه: أين سؤال عن المكان، وكان الله تعالى ولا مكان ولا زمان، وهو الآن كما كان.
And from Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, that he was asked: 'Where was our Lord before He created the Throne?' So Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'Where is a question about place, and Allah, exalted, existed while there was no place and no time, and He is now as He was.'
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is another transmitted proof (naqli dalil) from the fourth caliph, Ali ibn Abi Talib. When asked about Allah's location before the Throne, Ali does not answer with a spatial location. Instead, he reframes the question: 'Where' is a question about place (makan). But Allah existed while there was no place and no time. This implies that Allah's existence is not bound by spatial or temporal dimensions. Ali then adds 'He is now as He was,' meaning that Allah's state did not change after creating place and time. He does not acquire a location after creating the cosmos. This statement is a clear refutation of those who claim Allah physically sits on the Throne after creation.

Ja'far al-Sadiq's Three Conditions of True Tawhid
Nasafi transmits Ja'far al-Sadiq's definition of tawhid negating any relation to matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three negations that define true tawhid according to Ja'far al-Sadiq and why each negation is essential to avoid likening Allah to creation.

Core Idea
True tawhid negates any spatial or material relation with Allah.

In this lesson, we examine a powerful transmitted definition of tawhid from Ja'far al-Sadiq. He distills monotheism into three negations: Allah is not from something, not in something, and not on something. Each negation guards against a specific form of anthropomorphism that would undermine divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice how Ja'far al-Sadiq uses three concise negations to define tawhid.
The passage is short but densely packed with meaning.
2
Identify the three negations and their consequences
List the three negations: 'not from something', 'not in something', 'not on something'. For each, note the consequence if one were to affirm that attribute—created, limited, or needing support.
Each negation is followed by a conditional statement showing the error.
3
Reflect on why these negations are essential
Consider how each negation protects tawhid from associating Allah with created qualities. Why would describing Allah as 'from something' imply He is created? Discuss with a peer or journal your thoughts.
This links to the broader principle of tanzih (divine transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن جعفر الصادق رضي الله عنه أنه قال: التوحيد ثلاثة أحرف: أن تعرف أنه ليس من شيء، ولا في شيء، ولا على شيء، لأن مَنْ وصَفَه أنه من شيء فقد وصفه بأنه مخلوق فيكفر، ومن وصفه أنه في شيء فقد وصفه أنه محدود فيكفر، ومن وصفه أنه على شيء فقد وصفه أنه محتاج محمولٌ فيكفر.
And from Ja'far al-Sadiq, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: 'Tawhid (monotheism) consists of three letters: that you know He is not from something (min shay'), nor in something (fi shay'), nor on something (ala shay'). Because whoever describes Him as being from something has described Him as created, so he disbelieves; whoever describes Him as being in something has described Him as limited, so he disbelieves; and whoever describes Him as being on something has described Him as needing and carried, so he disbelieves.'
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a transmitted definition of tawhid from Ja'far al-Sadiq, a revered scholar. He explains tawhid in three negations: 1) Allah is not from something (min shay'), meaning He did not originate from any matter or element; if He were from something, He would be created (makhluq). 2) He is not in something (fi shay'), meaning He is not contained in any place or object; if He were, He would be limited (mahdud). 3) He is not on something (ala shay'), meaning He does not rest upon any surface; if He did, He would be in need of support (muhtaj) and carried (mahmul). Each case results in kufr because it likens Allah to created beings. This statement encapsulates the Ash'ari/Maturidi emphasis on tanzih (transcendence) and negates any spatial or material relation.

Key Terms
التوحيد
من شيء
في شيء
على شيء
مخلوق
محدود
محتاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think tawhid only means believing in one God, without requiring negation of spatial or material attributes.
Correction: Ja'far al-Sadiq shows that true tawhid also requires negating that Allah is from, in, or on anything, as these would imply createdness, limitation, or need.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
True tawhid requires not only affirming Allah's oneness but also negating any spatial or material relationship with creation.

The Three Negations of Tawheed
Ja'far al-Sadiq defines tawheed by three negations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that tawheed requires negating from Allah any origin, containment, or dependency, and how these negations protect against disbelief.

Core Idea
Tawheed is not only affirmation but also negation of limitations.

Ja'far al-Sadiq, a revered early scholar, presents a concise definition of tawheed using three negations. This approach emphasizes that true unity of Allah means removing any hint of createdness, limitation, or need. Read on to see how each negation guards against a specific form of disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to get the overall sense of the three negations and their consequences.
Notice the strong language: each negation leads to kufr if violated.
2
Examine each negation
In your mind, go through each of the three 'not's: not from anything, not in anything, not on anything. For each, see how describing Allah as such would imply a deficiency (created, limited, dependent).
3
Reflect on the manuscript variant
Consider the additional text from some manuscripts: 'without His having any need, and without His having settled upon it.' How does this reinforce the third negation?
This variant clarifies that 'on' implies settlement, which is also negated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن جعفر الصادق رضي الله عنه أنه قال: التوحيد ثلاثة أحرف: أن تعرف أنه ليس من شيء، ولا في شيء، ولا على شيء، لأن مَنْ وصَفَه أنه من شيء فقد وصفه بأنه مخلوق فيكفر، ومن وصفه أنه في شيء فقد وصفه أنه محدود فيكفر، ومن وصفه أنه على شيء فقد وصفه أنه محتاج محمولٌ فيكفر (۲). وردت في بعض الأصول الخطية لمتن الوصية وشرحها كما يلي: «من غير أن يكون له حاجة، ومن غير أن يكون استقر عليه.
And from Ja'far al-Sadiq, may Allah be pleased with him, that he said: 'Tawheed is three letters: that you know He is not from anything, nor in anything, nor on anything, because whoever describes Him as being from something has described Him as created and thus disbelieves; whoever describes Him as being in something has described Him as limited and thus disbelieves; whoever describes Him as being on something has described Him as in need and carried and thus disbelieves.' (2) And it occurs in some manuscripts of the text of al-Wasiyya and its commentary as follows: 'Without His having any need, and without His having settled upon it.'
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of tawheed from Ja'far al-Sadiq, expressed through three negations. 'Three letters' (ثلاثة أحرف) means three aspects or principles. The first: Allah is not from anything (ليس من شيء), meaning He is not originated from any substance. If He were from something, He would be a created being. The second: He is not in anything (لا في شيء), meaning He is not contained by any space or location. If He were contained, He would be limited. The third: He is not on anything (لا على شيء), meaning He does not rest upon or sit on any object. If He were on something, He would be in need of it for support and would be carried, which implies dependency. Each of these implications leads to disbelief (كفر) according to the speaker. The passage also includes a manuscript variant that adds that He has no need and does not settle. This emphasizes that the notion of 'settling' (استقرار) is also negated, further refuting anthropomorphic interpretations of Allah's 'istiwa' (establishing) over the Throne.

Key Terms

أحرف

لا في شيء
لا على شيء
مخلوق
محدود
محتاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'on something' (e.g., 'on the Throne') merely indicates a spatial direction like above, without implying need or dependency.
Correction: The passage clarifies that 'on something' implies need and being carried, which are incompatible with Allah’s self-sufficiency.

Checkpoint
According to Ja'far al-Sadiq, what does describing Allah as 'on something' imply?
A) That He is exalted
B) That He is limited
C) That He is in need and carried
D) That He is created

Key Takeaway
Tawheed requires negating from Allah any origin, location, or support.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you truly believe Allah is not limited by any place, does your prayer reflect that you are speaking to One who is present without being contained? What specific change can you make to remember this when you pray?
?
When you say 'Allah is the Creator,' do you ever subconsciously think of Him as being made of something or originating from something? How can you train your heart to negate that, starting today?

Bazdawi on the Metaphorical Ascension of Good Speech
Bazdawi interprets the verse about ascension metaphorically, denying spatial movement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Bazdawi interprets the verse about the ascension of good speech metaphorically, and how this argument refutes anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
Good speech ascends in honor, not in space — Allah is beyond direction.

Imam al-Bazdawi encounters a verse that might seem to suggest spatial movement towards Allah. But true tanzih (transcendence) demands careful interpretation. In this passage, he shows that the literal meaning is impossible for speech, and therefore the verse must be understood metaphorically. This lesson unpacks his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once without analysis. Let the author's reasoning come through.
Notice how Bazdawi begins by affirming Allah's eternal attributes.
2
Identify the literal rejection
Find the reasoning against the literal meaning. Why is 'ascend' impossible for speech?
He argues speech lacks the physical form needed for spatial movement.
3
Understand the metaphorical meaning
Bazdawi then provides the metaphorical interpretation: ascension means elevation in status and honor. See how he supports it with the sultan analogy.
The analogy shows closeness in rank, not physical proximity.
4
Connect to divine transcendence
Reflect on how this argument protects Allah's transcendence beyond space and direction.
This refutes those who claim Allah is in a physical direction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويقول الإمام البزدوي في كتابه أصول الدين ص ٤١ ما صورته: «الله تعالى على الصفة التي كان عليها قبل خلق العالم، أما قوله تعالى: ﴿إِلَيْهِ يَصْعَدُ الْكَلِمُ الطَّيِّبُ وَالْعَمَلُ الصَّلِحُ يَرْفَعُهُ [فاطر: ١٠] نقول: إن الحقيقة ساقطة العبرة ها هنا لأن الكلام لا يتصور منه الصعود حقيقة خصوصا كلام العباد فإنه لا بقاء له، فإذا لم يمكن العمل بحقيقة هذا الكلام فلم يعلم مراد الله تعالى من ذلك حقيقة فيصير بمعنى المجمل فلا يبقى حجة، ثم نقول: المراد منه والله أعلم هو المجازي على علو الكلم الطيب ويرفع صاحبه ويجعله عالي المقدار قريبًا من الله تعالى من حيث علو الحال والرفعة لا من حيث الذات كما في الشاهد يكون الإنسان قريبا من سلطان من حيث الرفعة والمكانة لا من حيث الجهة والمكان، فكذا هنا الله تعالى يرفع صاحب الكلم ويحمله على المنزلة، فيصعد بشرفه فإن الكلم قائم به... إلخ».
And Imam al-Bazdawi says in his book 'Usul al-Din' p. 41, the following: 'Allah Almighty is upon the attribute He was upon before the creation of the world. As for His saying, exalted is He: "To Him ascends good speech and righteous work raises it" [Fatir: 10], we say: The literal meaning is inapplicable here because speech cannot be conceived to ascend literally, especially the speech of servants, for it has no permanence. So when it is not possible to act upon the literal meaning of this speech, then the intended meaning of Allah Almighty from that is not known literally, so it becomes in the sense of a summary, so it does not remain a proof. Then we say: The intended meaning, and Allah knows best, is metaphorical: [it refers to] the loftiness of good speech, and He raises its doer and makes him high in rank, close to Allah Almighty in terms of loftiness of state and elevation, not in terms of essence, just as in our experience a person can be close to a sultan in terms of elevation and status, not in terms of direction and place. So likewise Allah Almighty raises the possessor of speech and conveys him to a high station, so he ascends in his honor, for the speech is attached to him... etc.'
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a proof from Imam al-Bazdawi arguing for a metaphorical interpretation of the verse 'إليه يصعد الكلم الطيب' (To Him ascends good speech). The argument proceeds in several steps: First, he asserts that Allah's attributes are eternal and unchanging, as He was before creation. Then he addresses the verse: the literal meaning (الحقيقة) of 'ascend' cannot apply here because speech, especially human speech, is not a physical entity that can move upwards. Moreover, it has no permanence. Since the literal meaning is impossible, we must understand that the literal intended meaning is not known; the verse becomes ambiguous (مجمل) and cannot be used as a proof for spatial direction. Therefore, the intended meaning is metaphorical (مجازي): it refers to the elevation of the speech in honor and the raising of the doer's rank, making him close to Allah in status, not in spatial proximity. Bazdawi uses an analogy: a person can be 'close' to a king in terms of honor and status without being physically near. Similarly, Allah raises the doer of good speech to a high station. The phrase 'فصاعد بشرفه' (so he ascends in his honor) emphasizes the figurative nature. This refutes anthropomorphists who take the verse literally to prove that Allah is in a direction.

Key Terms
الصعود
الحقيقة
المجاز
الكلم الطيب
الرفعة
المكانة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that metaphorical interpretation negates the literal truth of the verse.
Correction: Bazdawi shows that the literal meaning is impossible, so the metaphorical interpretation is the only valid understanding that preserves both the verse and divine transcendence.

Checkpoint

B) Because speech is not a physical entity that can move
C) Because the verse is abrogated
D) Because the Arabic language does not allow it

Key Takeaway
Bazdawi demonstrates that the ascension of good speech must be understood metaphorically to preserve Allah's transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Make a conscious effort today to replace any mental image of direction with a feeling of honor and sincerity.

?
Al-Bazdawi uses an analogy of closeness to a sultan in status, not in place. Evaluate your relationship with Allah: do you seek to be 'close' to Him primarily through rituals that give you a sense of physical proximity, or through actions that truly raise your honor and sincerity before Him? What one specific change in your intention or worship can you implement this week to focus on spiritual elevation?

Logical Proof that Allah is Not on the Throne
Imam al-Nasafi proves by logical division that Allah cannot be spatially on the Throne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that Allah cannot be spatially on the Throne, and why spatial attributes are impossible for the Eternal.

Core Idea
Allah cannot be on the Throne because any spatial relationship would entail division or finitude.

This lesson presents a rational proof from Imam al-Nasafi that demonstrates why Allah, being eternal and necessary, cannot occupy space or be located on the Throne. The proof uses a technique of exhaustive division to show that all possible spatial scenarios lead to impossibilities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the full translation. Pay attention to the logical structure.
Notice the three-fold division at the beginning.
2
Identify the three possibilities
The passage lists three possibilities regarding Allah's size relative to the Throne: larger, equal, or smaller. Find them in the text.
These are the branches of the logical division.
3
Understand why each is invalid
For each possibility, the author explains why it leads to an impossibility. Note the key reasons: division (tajazzu'), composition (tarkib), and finitude (hudud).
The commentary will help unpack each step.
4
Recognize the conclusion
The proof concludes that all possibilities are impossible, so Allah cannot be on the Throne. The final point about being limited and finite is a sign of creation.
This establishes tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن يكون أكبر من ساحة، وإما أن يكون مثل ساحة العرش ولم ينقص منها ولم يفضل عنها، وأما أن يكون أصغر منها. والأول باطل؛ لأنه يوجب كونه متبعضًا متجزيًّا، وكان بعض منه متمكنا على العرش وبعض منه غير متمكن، والقول بالتجزؤ باطل لأنه منافٍ للتوحيد على ما بينا، وكذا لو كان بمقدار العرش إذ لاقى كل جزء من أجزاء العرش جزءًا منه وكذا لو كان أصغر من العرش لما أن قدر ما يلاقيه من العرش متبعض فلاقي كل جزء منه جزءًا من الصانع وهو محال على الله تعالى لما مر من بيان منافاة التركيب والتبعض والتجزؤ على القديم، وكذا إن كان مساويًا لساحة العرش أو أصغر منه أو أكبر كان محدودًا متناهيا وهو من أمارات الحدث وثبوت شيء منها على القديم جل جلاله محال والله تعالى الموفق .
That He be larger than the area (of the Throne), or that He be equal to the area of the Throne not lacking from it nor exceeding it, or that He be smaller than it. The first is invalid because it necessitates that He be divided into parts and pieces, and some part of Him be settled on the Throne and some part not settled, and the statement of divisibility is invalid because it contradicts tawheed as we have explained. Similarly if He were equal to the measure of the Throne, then every part of the parts of the Throne would come into contact with a part of Him. And similarly if He were smaller than the Throne, because then the amount that contacts it from the Throne is divided, so each part of it contacts a part of the Maker, and that is impossible for Allah Almighty due to what has passed of the explanation of the incompatibility of composition, division, and divisibility with the Eternal. And similarly, whether He were equal to the area of the Throne, or smaller than it, or larger, He would be limited and finite, and that is among the signs of originatedness (hadath), and the establishment of any of these upon the Eternal, glorified is His majesty, is impossible. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a logical proof (dalil 'aqli) that Allah cannot be positioned on the Throne in a spatial sense. It uses exhaustive division (taqseem): if Allah were on the Throne, His size relative to the Throne would have to be one of three possibilities: larger, equal, or smaller. Each possibility is shown to entail impossibility. 1) Larger: would mean some parts of Allah are on the Throne and some are not, implying division (tajazzu') and parts (taba'ud), which contradicts divine oneness (tawheed). 2) Equal: would mean every part of the Throne contacts a part of Allah, again implying composition and divisibility. 3) Smaller: also entails contact with parts and thus divisibility of Allah. All three lead to Allah being limited and finite (mahdud mutanahi), which are marks of contingent beings (amarat al-hadath). Since Allah is eternal and necessary, none of these can apply. The conclusion is that it is impossible for Allah to be spatially on the Throne. The proof is built on the principle that any form of composition (tarkib) is impossible for the Divine.

Key Terms
العرش
التمكن
التبعض
التجزؤ
التركيب
المحدود
المتناهي
أمارات الحدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'being on the Throne' implies a specific size for Allah, but the argument shows it inevitably leads to absurdities regardless of size.
Correction: The proof shows that any size comparison leads to division or finitude, which are impossible for Allah. Thus, Allah is not spatially on the Throne in any sense.

Checkpoint
Why is the possibility that Allah is larger than the Throne considered invalid?
A) Because the Throne is infinite
B) Because it would imply that Allah is divided into parts
C) Because it would mean Allah is smaller than the Throne
D) Because it contradicts the verse about ascension

Key Takeaway
Allah is free from spatial location; any spatial relationship would entail composition or limitation, which are impossible for the Eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read a rational proof that Allah cannot be spatially located. But in your daily prayers, do you unconsciously picture Allah in a certain direction or place? What does this lesson demand you change about how you mentally orient yourself toward Him?
?
The proof says that any spatial relationship means limitation, and limitation is a sign of 'originatedness'. Where in your life have you been treating Allah as if He is limited or confined by your own expectations? Will you repent and realign your understanding?
?
Imam al-Nasafi used logic to protect tawheed. On the Day of Judgment, you will be asked about your belief in Allah's attributes. Are you content to hold a lazy understanding of 'above' without inner conviction, or will you actively seek the correct knowledge—even if it challenges your comfort?

Refuting Allah's Physical Relationship to the Throne
Nasafi enumerates three possibilities for Allah's size relative to the Throne and refutes each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attributing physical size or location to Allah relative to the Throne is impossible, based on the logical refutation of three possibilities.

Core Idea
Allah is not bounded by size or place; any such attribution implies composition and finitude.

Nasafi presents a powerful logical argument against anthropomorphism regarding Allah's relationship to the Throne. He considers three possible ways Allah could relate to the Throne if He were physically upon it—greater, equal, or smaller—and shows each leads to impossible consequences. This lesson walks through that argument and its implications for divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the logical structure of the argument emerge naturally.
Notice the use of conditional statements (if...then) and refutations.
2
Identify the three possibilities
The passage opens by listing three possibilities for Allah's size relative to the Throne. Write them down: greater, equal, smaller. These are the only logical possibilities if He were physically related.
The subsequent refutation applies to each one.
3
Understand the refutation of each possibility
For each possibility, Nasafi demonstrates an unacceptable consequence: division (taba'ud), composition (tajazzi), or finitude (mahdud). See how the first leads to parts being on and off the Throne, the second to each part touching, and the third also to touching of parts.
All these consequences contradict tawhid and the nature of the Eternal.
4
Recognize the common implication of finitude
Beyond the specific refutations, Nasafi points out that all three possibilities would make Allah bounded (mahdud) and finite (mutanahi), which are signs of contingency (hadath).
This seals the argument: size itself is incompatible with divinity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن يكون أكبر من ساحة، وإما أن يكون مثل ساحة العرش ولم ينقص منها ولم يفضل عنها، وأما أن يكون أصغر منها.
والأول باطل؛ لأنه يوجب كونه متبعضًا متجزيًّا، وكان بعض منه متمكنا على العرش وبعض منه غير متمكن، والقول بالتجزؤ باطل لأنه منافٍ للتوحيد على ما بينا، وكذا لو كان بمقدار العرش إذ لاقى كل جزء من أجزاء العرش جزءًا منه وكذا لو كان أصغر من العرش لما أن قدر ما يلاقيه من العرش متبعض فلاقي كل جزء منه جزءًا من الصانع وهو محال على الله تعالى لما مر من بيان منافاة التركيب والتبعض والتجزؤ على القديم، وكذا إن كان مساويًا لساحة العرش أو أصغر منه أو أكبر كان محدودًا متناهيا وهو من أمارات الحدث وثبوت شيء منها على القديم جل جلاله محال والله تعالى الموفق.
That He be greater than its area, or that He be equal to the area of the Throne without falling short of it or exceeding it, or that He be smaller than it. The first is false, because it necessitates His being divided into parts and having components, with some part of Him being established on the Throne and some part not established. And the claim of composition is false because it contradicts tawhid (monotheism), as we have explained. Likewise, if He were the size of the Throne, every part of the Throne would touch a part of Him. Likewise, if He were smaller than the Throne, the amount of the Throne that touches Him would be composed of parts, and thus each part of it would touch a part of the Creator, and that is impossible for Allah, due to what has passed of the explanation of the incompatibility of composition, division, and parts with the Eternal. Likewise, whether He is equal to the area of the Throne, smaller, or larger, He would be bounded and finite, which is a sign of contingency. Affirming any of that for the Eternal—glory be to Him—is impossible. And Allah is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage presents a logical argument against anthropomorphism. It begins by considering three possible relationships between Allah and the Throne if He is physically upon it: He is larger than the Throne, equal to it, or smaller. Each possibility is refuted. The first (larger) would imply that Allah is composed of parts (taba'ud), with some parts on the Throne and others not—this violates tawhid. The second (equal) would imply that each part of the Throne touches a corresponding part of Allah. The third (smaller) would similarly imply a touching of parts between a portion of the Throne and a portion of Allah. All these scenarios involve composition (tarkib) and division (tajazzi), which are impossible for the Eternal (al-Qadim). Moreover, any of the three possibilities would mean that Allah is bounded and finite (mahdud mutanahi), which is a characteristic of contingent beings (hawadith). Thus, the very question of size relative to the Throne is incoherent for Allah.

Key Terms
التبعض
التجزي
التركيب
المحدود
المتناهي
القديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that affirming Allah's 'istiwa' (establishing) over the Throne requires a physical size or location.
Correction: This argument shows that any physical relationship (greater, equal, smaller) leads to composition and finitude, which are impossible for Allah. Hence, 'istiwa' must be understood in a manner befitting His majesty, without physicality.

Checkpoint

A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Allah is not subject to physical dimensions; any attempt to assign a size relative to the Throne leads to logical contradictions of composition and finitude.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Refuting the Jahmiyyah: Allah Exists Without Place or Direction
Nasafi introduces a chapter, presents the Jahmiyyah's claim with proof texts, and starts the refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Jahmiyyah's claim that Allah is everywhere, the verses they used to support it, and the method of interpreting them in a way that preserves Allah's transcendence.

Core Idea
The Jahmiyyah's proof texts do not prove spatial location.

Nasafi opens a new chapter to establish a central tenet of Sunni theology: Allah is not confined to place or direction. The Jahmiyyah, an early sect, insisted otherwise, citing Quranic verses that speak of Allah being 'in the heaven' or 'with' people. In this lesson, we examine their claim and the scriptural evidence they presented, and we begin to see how Nasafi refutes their misinterpretations.

Guided Path
1
Read the chapter title and introduction
Notice the clear statement of the topic: proving Allah exists without a place and negating direction. This sets the stage for the refutation.
The title is a direct address to the Jahmiyyah's position.
2
Identify the Jahmiyyah's claim and their proofs
The passage explicitly states: 'The Jahmiyyah said: Allah is in every place.' Then it lists five Quranic verses they adduced. Read each verse carefully.
These verses use the prepositions 'in' (fi) and 'with' (ma'a), which the Jahmiyyah took literally.
3
Observe the beginning of Nasafi's answer
Nasafi starts his refutation with the first verse, explaining that its intended meaning (taqdiruhu) is that Allah is the God of those in heaven and earth, not that He is spatially located there.
This is the method of ta'wil (interpretation) – a key tool in Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
في إثبات أن الله موجود بلا مكان ونفي الجهة عن الله تعالى
قالت الجهمية: إن الله تعالى بكل مكان، واحتجوا بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ الَّذِي فِي السَّمَاءِ إِلَهُ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَهُ وَهُوَ الْحَكِيمُ الْعَلِيمُ ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَهُوَ اللَّهُ في السَّمَوَاتِ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ اللَّهَ مَعَ الَّذِينَ اتَّقُوا وَالَّذِينَ هُم مُحْسِنُونَ ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿مَا يَكُونُ مِن نَّجْوَى ثَلَاثَةٍ إِلَّا هُوَ رَابِعُهُمْ وَلَا خَمْسَةٍ إِلَّا هُوَ سَادِسُهُمْ وَلَا أَدْنَى مِن ذَلِكَ وَلَا أَكْثَرَ إِلَّا هُوَ مَعَهُمْ أَيْنَ مَا كَانُوا ﴾ وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ مَعَكُمْ أَيْنَ مَا كُنتُمْ ﴾.
والجواب عن قوله تعالى ﴿وَهُوَ الَّذِي فِي السَّمَاءِ إِلَهُ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَهَ ) أي : تقديره
Chapter on proving that Allah exists without a place and negating direction from Allah Almighty. The Jahmiyyah said: Allah Almighty is in every place. And they adduced His statement: 'It is He who is God in the heaven and God in the earth, and He is the Wise, the Knowing' [al-Zukhruf: 84], and His statement: 'And He is Allah in the heavens and in the earth' [al-An'am: 3], and His statement: 'Indeed Allah is with those who fear Him and those who are doers of good' [al-Nahl: 128], and His statement: 'There is no secret conversation of three but He is their fourth, nor of five but He is their sixth, nor less than that nor more but He is with them wherever they are' [al-Mujadilah: 7], and His statement: 'And He is with you wherever you are' [al-Hadid: 4]. The answer concerning His statement 'It is He who is God in the heaven and God in the earth' is: Its intended meaning is...
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage opens a new chapter. The title announces the topic: proving that Allah exists without a place (bila makan) and negating direction (jihah) from Him. The author then presents the claim of the Jahmiyyah, an early sect that held Allah is physically present in every place. They support their view with five Quranic verses that mention Allah being 'in the heaven and the earth' or 'with' people. The author begins the refutation by taking the first verse and explaining that its intended meaning (taqdiruhu) is that Allah is the God of those in heaven and earth, not that He is spatially located there. The answer is incomplete in this page, but the clear method is to interpret these verses in a way that befits Allah's transcendence.

نفي الجهة
بلا مكان
التقدير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah is physically present in every place based on verses with 'in' and 'with'.
Correction: These verses are interpreted metaphorically: they refer to Allah's knowledge, power, and sovereignty, not spatial indwelling.

Checkpoint

B) Jahmiyyah
C) Mu'tazilah

Key Takeaway
The Jahmiyyah's scriptural proofs for Allah being everywhere are valid only if taken literally; Sunni theologians interpret them as references to Allah's sovereignty and knowledge.

?
This passage teaches that even sincere reading of the Quran can lead to grave mistakes without proper methodology. What habits do you have in reading the Quran that might lead you to misunderstand Allah's attributes? Will you commit to learning the principles of tafsir?

Refuting the Jahmiyya: Interpreting the Verses
Nasafi presents Jahmiyya proof texts and their reinterpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahl al-Sunna interpret the Quranic verses that the Jahmiyya used to claim Allah is everywhere, distinguishing between physical presence and divine knowledge and power.

Core Idea
Allah is everywhere by knowledge and power, not by essence.

The Jahmiyya sect claimed that Allah is physically present in every place, citing several Quranic verses. This lesson introduces their proof texts and presents the correct Sunni interpretation that upholds Allah's transcendence without denying His omnipresence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Jahmiyya claim and proof verses
Start by reading the passage where the Jahmiyya state their position and list five Quranic verses they believe support their view.
These verses include references to Allah being 'in heaven' and 'with you'.
2
Study the author's response for each verse
For each verse, the author gives a reinterpretation that shifts meaning from physical location to divine attributes like knowledge, decree, and power.
Notice how 'in heaven' is explained as 'His decree and management'.
3
Identify the pattern in the interpretations
All reinterpretations avoid implying spatial confinement and instead point to Allah's knowledge and power being everywhere.
For example, 'He is with you' means 'by knowledge'.
4
Reflect on the theological necessity
Ask yourself why this reinterpretation is crucial for preserving tawhid and avoiding anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قالت الجهمية: إن الله تعالى بكل مكان، واحتجوا بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ الَّذِي فِي السَّمَاءِ إِلَهُ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَهُ وَهُوَ الْحَكِيمُ الْعَلِيمُ ﴾ [الزخرف: ٨٤] وقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَهُوَ اللَّهُ في السَّمَوَاتِ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ ﴾ [الأنعام: ۳] وقوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ اللَّهَ مَعَ الَّذِينَ اتَّقُوا وَالَّذِينَ هُم تُحْسِنُونَ ﴾ [النحل: ۱۲۸] وقوله تعالى: ﴿مَا يَكُونُ مِن نَّجْوَى ثَلَثَةٍ إِلَّا هُوَ رَابِعُهُمْ وَلَا خَمْسَةٍ إِلَّا هُوَ سَادِسُهُمْ وَلَا أَدْنَى مِن ذَلِكَ وَلَا أَكْثَرَ إِلَّا هُوَ مَعَهُمْ أَيْنَ مَا كَانُوا ﴾ [المجادلة: ۷] وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ مَعَكُمْ أَيْنَ مَا كُنتُمْ ﴾ [الحديد: ٤].
والجواب عن قوله تعالى ﴿وَهُوَ الَّذِي فِي السَّمَاءِ إِلَهُ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَهُ ) أي : تقديره وتدبيره. وقوله تعالى: أَمِنْتُم مِّن فِي السَّمَاءِ أَن يَخْسِفَ بِكُمُ الْأَرْضَ ) [الملك: ١٦] أى أمنتم ممن ظهرت آثار قدرته في السماء.
وقوله: ﴿مَا يَكُونُ مِن نَّجْوَى ثَلَثَةِ إِلَّا هُوَ رَابِعُهُمْ ) يعني علمه.
وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ مَعَكُمْ أَيْنَ مَا كُنتُمْ ﴾ أي بالعلم.
ولأنا لو قلنا بأنه في المكان يؤدي إلى أمر قبيح، لأنه لا يخلو إما أن يكون كله بكل مكان، أو بكلِّ مكانٍ من طريق الأجزاء، أو بمكان دون مكان.
وباطل أن يكون كله بكلِّ مكان، لأنه يؤدي إلى أن يكون إلهين اثنين، لا أن يكون إلهاً واحداً، والإله واحد، وباطل أن يكون بكل مكان بطريق الأجزاء، لأن مَنْ وَصَفَ الله تعالى بالأجزاء فإنه يكفر، وباطل أن يكون بمكان دون مكان، لأنه يحتاج إلى الانتقال وهو من صفات المخلوقين وأمارات المحدثين، والله تعالى منزّه عن ذلك.
Chapter on proving that God exists without place and negating direction from God Almighty. The Jahmiyya said: God Almighty is everywhere, and they adduced as proof His saying: 'And He it is who in heaven is God and on earth is God, and He is the Wise, the Knower' (43:84); and His saying: 'And He is God in the heavens and on earth' (6:3); and His saying: 'Indeed Allah is with those who fear Him and those who do good' (16:128); and His saying: 'There is no secret conversation of three but He is their fourth, nor of five but He is their sixth, nor less than that nor more but He is with them wherever they are' (58:7); and His saying: 'And He is with you wherever you are' (57:4). The answer concerning His saying 'And He it is who in heaven is God and on earth is God' means: His decree and management. And His saying: 'Do you feel secure that He who is in heaven will cause the earth to swallow you?' (67:16) means: Do you feel secure from the one whose effects of power appear in heaven? And His saying: 'There is no secret conversation of three but He is their fourth' means: His knowledge. And His saying: 'And He is with you wherever you are' means: by knowledge. And because if we said that He is in a place, it would lead to an odious thing; for inevitably either He is wholly in every place, or in every place by way of parts, or in a place without a place. It is false that He is wholly in every place, because it leads to there being two gods, not one God, and God is one. And it is false that He is in every place by way of parts, because whoever describes God Almighty with parts disbelieves. And it is false that He is in a place without a place, because He would need movement, which is an attribute of created beings and a sign of originated things, and God Almighty is free of that.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage refutes the Jahmiyya claim that Allah is in every place. The author first cites their proof texts—five Quranic verses that seem to suggest Allah's presence in heaven, on earth, or with people. Then he provides the correct interpretation: 'He who is in heaven is God' means His decree and management; 'Do you feel secure from Him who is in heaven' means from the one whose effects of power appear in heaven; 'He is their fourth' and 'He is with you' both refer to His knowledge, not His physical presence. After scriptural interpretation, the author presents a rational argument: if Allah were in a place, three possibilities exist—He is wholly in every place, partially in every place, or in a specific place. The first is false because it implies two gods; the second is false because parts imply composition, which is disbelief; the third is false because it requires movement, an attribute of created beings. Thus, Allah is free of place and direction.

بكل مكان
العلم
القدرة
التقدير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verses that say Allah is 'in heaven' or 'with you' mean He is physically present in those places.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna interpret such verses as referring to Allah's knowledge, power, and decree, not His physical location.

Checkpoint

A) Allah is physically present with you everywhere
B) Allah knows everything that happens
C) Allah's power appears in heaven
D) Allah's decree and management

Key Takeaway
Allah is everywhere by His knowledge and power, not by His essence.

The Rational Argument: The Impossibility of Place for God
Nasafi presents a rational trilemma proving Allah cannot be in a place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational trilemma that disproves the possibility of God being in a place, and why each of the three possibilities is false.

Core Idea
Three impossibilities prove Allah cannot occupy any location.

After addressing the scriptural proofs, Nasafi presents a rational argument. He outlines three logical possibilities if Allah were in a place—each leads to an absurdity. This lesson unpacks that trilemma and shows why Allah must be free from direction and space.

Guided Path
1
Read the trilemma statement
The author presents three possibilities for how Allah could be in a place: wholly everywhere, partially everywhere, or in a specific place.
These are exhaustive and mutually exclusive.
2
Understand the refutation of each possibility
Each possibility is shown to be false: wholly everywhere implies two gods; partially implies composition; in a specific place implies movement.
Note the specific consequences mentioned.
3
Connect to the principle of tawhid and transcendence
The refutations preserve tawhid (oneness), avoid anthropomorphism, and affirm Allah's freedom from created attributes.
4
Reflect on the complementary nature of rational and scriptural evidence
This rational argument supports the scriptural reinterpretation from the previous lesson.

The Logical Refutation of Allah Being in a Place
Imam Nasafi refutes three logical possibilities of Allah being in a place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why it is logically impossible for Allah to be in a place, as demonstrated by Imam Nasafi's three-part refutation.

Core Idea
Allah being in a place leads to absurdities that contradict His oneness, simplicity, and transcendence.

This lesson presents a powerful logical argument from Imam Nasafi that refutes any notion of Allah occupying space. By examining three possible ways something could be in a place, he shows each leads to an impossibility. This establishes the Islamic doctrine that Allah is transcendent beyond location.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the literal translation to get a general sense of the argument.
Notice the three possibilities are presented as exhaustive: either whole, by parts, or in a specific place.
2
Identify the three possibilities
List the three ways something could be 'in a place' according to the passage. Write them down in your own words.
They are: (1) entirely in every place, (2) by parts in every place, (3) in a particular place only.
3
Understand each refutation
For each possibility, note the specific reason why it is false. Connect each reason to an attribute of Allah (oneness, simplicity, transcendence).
The reasons are: (1) implies multiple gods, (2) implies parts (composition), (3) implies movement.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
After seeing all three rebuttals, conclude that Allah cannot be in any place. This affirms the doctrine of Allah's transcendence above spatial attributes.
This argument is a cornerstone of Islamic theology regarding Allah's relationship to creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأنا لو قلنا بأنه في المكان يؤدي إلى أمر قبيح، لأنه لا يخلو إما أن يكون كله بكل مكان، أو بكلِّ مكانٍ من طريق الأجزاء، أو بمكان دون مكان.
وباطل أن يكون كله بكلِّ مكان، لأنه يؤدي إلى أن يكون إلهين اثنين، لا أن يكون إلهاً واحداً، والإله واحد، وباطل أن يكون بكل مكان بطريق الأجزاء، لأن مَنْ وَصَفَ الله تعالى بالأجزاء فإنه يكفر، وباطل أن يكون بمكان دون مكان، لأنه يحتاج إلى الانتقال وهو من صفات المخلوقين وأمارات المحدثين، والله تعالى منزّه عن ذلك.
And if we were to say that He is in a place, it would lead to an ugly matter, because it is unavoidable that either He is entirely in every place, or in every place in terms of parts, or in a place without (other) places. It is false that He is entirely in every place, because that would lead to two gods, not one God, and God is one. And it is false that He is in every place by way of parts, because whoever describes Allah with parts becomes a disbeliever. And it is false that He is in a place without (other) places, because He would then need to move, which is a characteristic of created beings and a sign of originated things, and Allah is exalted above that.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a proof refuting the notion that Allah is in a place. The author presents a threefold classification: either Allah is entirely in every place, or in every place by parts, or in one specific place. He then refutes each possibility: being entirely in every place would imply multiple gods (pantheism), being by parts implies composition and thus disbelief, and being in one place implies need for movement, which is a property of contingent beings. Thus, Allah is transcendent above location.

Key Terms
مكان
أجزاء
انتقال
مخلوقين
محدثين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some Muslims believe that Allah is literally in the sky or on the Throne in a spatial sense.
Correction: This passage shows that spatial location implies absurdities; therefore, such expressions must be interpreted metaphorically, affirming Allah's transcendence.

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is it false to say Allah is entirely in every place?
A) Because that would imply He is divided
B) Because that would lead to multiple gods
C) Because that requires movement
D) Because that makes Him limited

Key Takeaway
Allah is not in a place because any form of spatial location leads to logical contradictions incompatible with His oneness, simplicity, and transcendence.
