Refuting Literal Spatial Interpretation of Verses
Refutes anthropomorphic interpretation of verses using eternal vs. created distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the literal interpretation of spatial verses like 'So wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' is rationally impossible, based on the distinction between the eternal Creator and the created world.

Core Idea
Allah is eternal; creation is limited — literal direction is impossible.

This passage from Imam Nasafi tackles a critical point: how to understand verses that seem to assign a direction or place to Allah. Many groups mistakenly take them literally, leading to anthropomorphism. The author uses a rational argument rooted in the attributes of Allah and creation to show why such literalism is incoherent. Let's follow his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and English translation. Notice the rhetorical question and the two key verses mentioned.
The argument hinges on the concept of qadim vs. muhdath.
2
Identify the absurdity
The author points out that if Allah were literally in heaven, He would have been nowhere before heaven's creation. This is a logical contradiction for the Eternal.
This is a classic kalam argument for tanzih.
3
Reflect on the method
Understand that such verses must be interpreted in a way befitting Allah’s majesty (tanzih). This is the methodology of Ahl al-Sunna.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله تعالى: فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ اللَّهِ فهل معنى ذلك أن المصلّي أينما ولى وجهه يكون مقابلاً لمكان الله ؟ تعالى الله عما يقولون ، وكذلك قوله: وَهُوَ الَّذِي فِي السَّمَاءِ إِلَهُ وَفِي الْأَرْضِ إِلَهُ وما شابهها من آياتٍ وأخبار فإنها تُحمل على ما يليق بالله جل جلاله. ولا يخفى فساد قول من يقول إن الله تعالى في السماء حقيقة، لأن الله تعالى قديم، والسماء محدثة محدودة، فإن كان الله في السماء بالمعنى الحقيقي فأين كان قبل أن يخلق السماء؟ ففساد هذا ظاهر لكل عاقل.
The statement of Allah, Most High: So wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah. Does that mean that the one praying, wherever he turns his face, he is facing a place of Allah? Exalted is Allah above what they say. Likewise His statement: And He is the one who is God in the heaven and God on the earth, and similar verses and reports are interpreted in a manner befitting Allah, the Mighty and Majestic. And the corruption of the saying of those who say that Allah, Most High, is literally in the heaven is not hidden, because Allah, Most High, is eternal (qadīm), and the heaven is created (muḥdath) and limited (maḥdūd). If Allah were literally in the heaven, then where was He before He created the heaven? The corruption of this is apparent to every rational person.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of anthropomorphism (tashbīh) and the literal interpretation of certain verses. It begins by quoting the verse 'So wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' and rhetorically asks: does that mean the worshipper faces a place of Allah? No, Allah is exalted above that. Then it mentions the verse 'He is God in the heaven and God on the earth' and states that such verses must be interpreted in a way that befits Allah's majesty (tanzīh). Then it argues against those who say Allah is literally in heaven: since Allah is eternal (qadīm) and the heaven is created and limited, if Allah were in heaven He would have been contained by a created thing, and where was He before heaven's creation? This is absurd to any rational person.

Key Terms
وجه الله
التنزيه
التشبيه
قديم
محدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'face of Allah' implies a physical direction or place.
Correction: The passage shows this is rationally impossible because Allah is eternal and not limited by created places.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the literal interpretation that Allah is in heaven?
A) Heaven is too small
B) Allah is eternal, heaven is created and limited
C) The verse is abrogated
D) The Prophet forbade it

Key Takeaway
Allah’s eternality (qidam) and creation’s contingency (huduth) refute any literal spatial interpretation of verses.

Ibn Mas'ud's narration records the Prophet's own affirmation of seeing Allah on Mi'raj.

The question of whether the Prophet Muhammad saw his Lord is a key topic in Islamic theology. This lesson presents a direct narration from a trusted companion, Ibn Mas'ud, who asked the Prophet himself. The answer is clear and unequivocal, providing a foundation for understanding the possibility of divine vision.

Response to the Objection from 'Lan Tarani'
The author refutes the objection from 'Lan tarani' by reinterpreting the particle 'lan'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the verse 'Lan tarani' does not disprove the possibility of seeing Allah, and how the Arabic particle 'lan' is used for emphasis and temporal limitation rather than eternal negation.

Core Idea
The particle 'lan' does not mean forever; it is for emphasis and limited time.

In this passage, the author tackles a key objection raised against the possibility of seeing Allah in the afterlife: the Quranic verse 'You will not see Me' (7:143). Some argue that the word 'lan' in Arabic indicates an eternal negation. The author refutes this by examining the actual usage of 'lan' in the Qur'an, showing that it is used for emphasis and temporal limitation, not eternal negation. Through two powerful examples, the author demonstrates that the meaning of 'lan' depends on context.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the author's initial response
Start by reading the first sentence where the author presents the objection from verse 7:143 and then says 'We do not concede that the word 'lan' indicates eternity'. Notice the direct refutation.
2
Examine the first Quranic example from Surah al-Baqara
The author quotes verse 2:95 where Allah says disbelievers will never wish for death, but later in 43:77 they do wish for it. This shows 'lan' does not mean eternal negation.
Notice the addition of 'abadan' for emphasis.
3
Examine the second example from Surah Maryam
Maryam says she will not speak to anyone today. The 'lan' here is clearly limited to that day. This reinforces the point.
4
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that 'lan' is for emphasis and temporal limitation, not eternity. Relate this back to the original verse: it does not preclude seeing Allah forever.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما قوله تعالى: ﴿لَن تَرانِي﴾ قلنا: لا نُسَلّمُ بأنَّ كلمةَ (لن) للتأبيد، بل هي للتأكيد وللتأقيت، وهذا لأن الله تعالى أخبر أنَّ الكفار لا يتمنون الموت بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَن يَتَمَنَّوْهُ أَبَدًا بِمَا قَدَّمَتْ أَيْدِيهِمْ﴾ [البقرة: 95] ثم أخبر أنهم يتمنون الموت بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَنَادَوْا يَا مَالِكُ لِيَقْضِ عَلَيْنَا رَبُّكَ قَالَ إِنَّكُم مَّاكِثُونَ﴾ فَعُلِمَ أنَّ كلمة (لن) ليس للتأييد. وكذلك قوله تعالى خبرًا عن مريم: ﴿إِنِّي نَذَرْتُ لِلرَّحْمَنِ صَوْمًا فَلَنْ أُكَلِّمَ الْيَوْمَ إِنسِيًّا﴾ [مريم: 26] ومع هذا لا يقتضي التأييد.
As for His saying, Exalted is He, 'You will not see Me' [al-A'raf 7:143], we say: We do not concede that the word 'lan' indicates eternity; rather it is for emphasis and for temporal limitation. This is because Allah, Exalted is He, informed that the disbelievers do not wish for death in His saying, Exalted is He: 'And they will never wish for it ever, because of what their hands have forwarded' [al-Baqara 2:95]; then He informed that they will wish for death in His saying, Exalted is He: 'And they will cry: O Malik, let your Lord make an end of us. He will say: Indeed, you are abiding' [az-Zukhruf 43:77]. Thus it was known that the word 'lan' is not for eternity. And similarly His saying, Exalted is He, relating from Maryam: 'Indeed, I have vowed to the Most Merciful a fast, so I will not speak today to any human' [Maryam 19:26]; yet this does not necessitate eternity.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objection is based on the verse 'Lan tarani' (You will not see Me), which seems to negate the possibility of seeing Allah forever. The author refutes this by arguing that the Arabic particle 'lan' does not inherently indicate eternal negation. Rather, it is used for emphasis and temporal limitation. To prove this, the author provides two Quranic examples. First, in Surah al-Baqara verse 95, Allah says that the disbelievers will never (lan) wish for death, and the word 'abadan' (ever) is added for emphasis. But in Surah az-Zukhruf verse 77, Allah informs that they will subsequently wish for death, showing that the negation was not eternal. Second, the verse from Maryam where Maryam says she will not (lan) speak to anyone today, yet this is clearly only for that day. Thus the original verse does not prove eternal negation of seeing Allah.

Key Terms
لن
التأبيد
التأقيت
التأكيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Arabic particle 'lan' always indicates eternal negation.
Correction: 'Lan' is used for emphasis and temporal limitation; its meaning is determined by context, as shown by Quranic examples.

Checkpoint
What does the author argue about the particle 'lan' in the verse 'Lan tarani'?
A) It means eternal negation
B) It indicates emphasis and temporal limitation
C) It is only used for negation in the past
D) It means 'never' in all contexts

Key Takeaway
The verse 'Lan tarani' does not prove that seeing Allah is impossible forever; the particle 'lan' is contextual and does not imply eternal negation.

Distinguishing Idrak from Ru'ya in the Verse 'La Tudrikuhu al-Absar'
The author distinguishes between 'idrak' and 'ru'ya' in response to a verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key distinction between idrak (comprehension) and ru'ya (vision) and why the verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' does not negate the possibility of seeing Allah.

Core Idea
The verse negates comprehension, not vision—a crucial theological distinction.

This lesson examines a common objection to the Ash'ari belief that Allah can be seen in the afterlife. The verse 'Vision does not comprehend Him' (al-An'am 6:103) is cited. The response hinges on understanding that 'idrak' and 'ru'ya' are not synonyms. Let's explore this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the English translation. Notice the concise style. The author directly addresses the objection.
2
Understand the objection
The objection is based on the verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar'. Some argue this means Allah cannot be seen. Recognize that this is a scriptural challenge to the belief in ru'ya.
3
Identify the author's response
The author distinguishes between idrak (comprehension) and ru'ya (vision). He states that the verse only negates idrak, not ru'ya. This is the core distinction.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
This distinction allows Ash'aris to affirm that Allah can be seen in the Hereafter (ru'ya) while maintaining that His essence cannot be fully comprehended (idrak).
Think about why this distinction is necessary for a coherent theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ﴾ قلنا: النصُّ يقتضي انتفاء الإدراك، ولكن لا يقتضي انتفاء الرؤية.
As for His saying, Exalted is He: 'Vision does not comprehend Him' [al-An'am 6:103], we say: The text necessitates the negation of comprehension (idrak), but it does not necessitate the negation of vision (ru'ya).
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This is another objection-and-answer. The objection cites the verse 'Sights do not comprehend Him' (la tudrikuhu al-absar). The author responds by making a crucial theological distinction between two concepts: idrak (comprehension, perception, or grasping in full) and ru'ya (vision, seeing). He argues that the verse only negates idrak, not ru'ya. This distinction is a standard Ash'ari response: seeing Allah is possible in the afterlife, but fully comprehending Him is impossible because He is infinite.

Key Terms
الإدراك
الرؤية
الأبصار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'La tudrikuhu al-absar' proves that Allah cannot be seen at all.
Correction: The verse only negates idrak (comprehension), not ru'ya (vision). Ash'aris hold that seeing Allah is possible but comprehending Him is not.

Checkpoint

B) Idrak (comprehension)
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The verse negates idrak, not ru'ya—a key distinction in Ash'ari theology.

Limiting the Scope of the Hadith of Aisha
The author limits the hadith's negation to this world only.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how kalam scholars limit the scope of a textual proof (dalil naqli) to a specific context, using the hadith of Aisha about seeing Allah as an example.

Core Idea
A text may negate something in one context but not another.

In this short but powerful passage, the author tackles an objection based on a hadith narrated by Aisha. The objector claims that the Prophet said he did not see his Lord, implying that seeing Allah is impossible altogether. The author’s response is a masterclass in textual precision: he points out that the hadith only denies seeing in this world, not in the afterlife. This lesson will help you appreciate how careful attention to the scope of a proof can resolve apparent conflicts.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author first mentions the hadith (حديث عائشة) and then gives his answer (قلنا).
The structure is: reference to the objection, then the response.
2
Identify the key terms
Find the words for 'this world' (الدنيا) and 'afterlife' (الآخرة). These two terms are central to the argument.
The author contrasts the two realms to limit the hadith's scope.
3
Understand the logical move
The author uses a rhetorical question: 'Did you claim that he is not seen in the afterlife?' This challenges the objector to prove an extension beyond the text's explicit wording.
This is a common kalam technique: restricting the literal meaning to its immediate context.
4
Apply the lesson
Think of other examples where a text might be misapplied if its scope is not carefully considered. Consider how this principle protects theological claims from overgeneralization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حديث عائشة رضي الله عنها، قلنا: النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أخبر أنه لا يُرى في الدنيا، ولكن لم قلتم بأنه لا يُرى في الآخرة؟
As for the hadith of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, we say: The Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, informed that he is not seen in this world, but did you claim that he is not seen in the afterlife?
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage responds to an objection based on a hadith narrated by Aisha, which is often interpreted to mean that the Prophet did not see his Lord. The author points out that the hadith only denies the vision of Allah in this world (fi al-dunya), not in the afterlife (al-akhira). The rhetorical question 'why did you claim that he is not seen in the afterlife?' challenges the objector to provide evidence for extending the negation to the next life. This is a typical kalam argument: limiting the scope of a text.

Key Terms
حديث عائشة
الدنيا
الآخرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith of Aisha proves that the Prophet never saw Allah, neither in this world nor in the afterlife.
Correction: The hadith only mentions 'this world' (al-dunya). The author reminds us that the text does not address the afterlife, so it cannot be used as evidence against seeing Allah in Paradise.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the hadith of Aisha negate?
A) Seeing Allah in this world
B) Seeing Allah in the afterlife
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
A textual proof must be applied only within its explicit scope; it does not automatically extend to other contexts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The author restricts the hadith to this world only. Is there a belief you hold that might be based on extending a text beyond its intended limits? How will you verify its true scope today?

Response to the Direction Objection
The author refutes an objection that vision of Allah implies direction by distinguishing conditions of the seen object.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection that seeing Allah would require Him to be in a direction, by distinguishing the condition of the seen object.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah does not need a direction because Allah is beyond spatial constraints.

In the previous lessons, the author has defended the possibility and actuality of seeing Allah in the afterlife. Now he addresses a key objection: that affirming vision would force us to say Allah is located in a direction. This objection is common among those who think all vision requires physical location. The author's response is sharp and logical, showing that the objection only applies if the seen object is in a direction, which is not the case for Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: objection, conditional reply, and concluding analogy.
The author uses concise language; each part is important.
2
Identify the two scenarios
The author presents two possibilities: if the seen object is in a direction, and if it is not. See how he concedes the first but denies the second for Allah.
This conditional reasoning is central to the refutation.
3
Reflect on the distinction between idrak and ru'ya
The author restates that negation of comprehensive perception (idrak) does not negate vision (ru'ya), recalling an earlier discussion about knowledge (ilm).
This reinforces that Allah can be seen without being fully comprehended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله: لو قلنا يُرى يؤدي إلى إثبات الجهة، قلنا: متى؟ إذا كان المرئي في الجهة أم إذا لم يكن. الأول: مسلَّم. والثاني: ممنوع، ولكن المرئي ههنا ليس في الجهة فلا يلزم من ضرورة انتفاء الإدراك انتفاء الرؤية وصار هذا كما قلنا في العلم.
As for his saying: 'If we say that He is seen, it leads to affirming direction (jiha),' we say: When? If the seen object is in a direction, or if it is not. The first: conceded. The second: denied. But the seen object here is not in a direction, so it does not follow from the necessity of negating comprehension (idrak) the negation of vision (ru'ya). And this is as we said regarding knowledge (ilm).
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This is the fourth objection-and-answer. The objector argues that affirming the vision of Allah would imply that Allah is located in a direction (jiha), which is impossible for Him. The author replies by distinguishing between two scenarios: if the seen object is in a direction, then seeing would imply direction, but if it is not, then it does not. The author asserts that Allah is not in a direction, so seeing Him does not entail direction. He then restates the earlier distinction between idrak and ru'ya, and concludes that negation of idrak does not imply negation of ru'ya, just as they had argued regarding knowledge (ilm) — likely a reference to a prior discussion where they distinguished between knowing God and comprehending Him completely.

Key Terms
الجهة
المرئي
الإدراك
الرؤية
العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All vision requires the object to be in a direction.
Correction: Vision only implies direction if the seen object itself is in a direction. Since Allah is not in a direction, seeing Him does not entail direction.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what condition would make seeing something imply a direction?
A) The seer is in a direction
B) The seen object is in a direction
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Seeing Allah does not imply He is in a direction, because the entailment only holds if the seen object is in a direction, and Allah transcends direction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about seeing Allah in the afterlife, do you unconsciously picture a direction or location for Him? How does the author's logical distinction challenge that mental image? What specific step will you take to purify your concept of Allah from spatial limitations?

Nasafi's Responses to Three Objections Against Seeing Allah
Nasafi answers three objections against the vision of Allah in the Hereafter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi refutes three common objections to the Sunni belief that believers will see Allah in the Hereafter by distinguishing between idrak and ru'ya, limiting the hadith to this world, and denying that vision implies direction.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah in the Hereafter is possible because vision is not the same as comprehension.

Imam Nasafi defends the Sunni doctrine of ru'ya (seeing Allah) in the Hereafter by addressing three key objections. Each objection arises from a misunderstanding of scriptural texts or logical implications. This lesson walks you through his concise yet powerful responses, clarifying the distinctions between idrak and ru'ya, the scope of hadith, and the concept of direction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the literal translation. Notice the three objections introduced by 'أما قوله' and 'أما حديث' and 'وأما قوله'.
The passage begins with an unclear reference, but the three objections are clear.
2
Identify the three objections
Find each objection: (1) the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار', (2) the hadith of Aisha, (3) the argument that seeing implies direction. Notice how Nasafi responds to each.
Each response begins with 'قلنا' (we say).
3
Understand the first response: idrak vs ru'ya
Nasafi says the verse negates idrak (comprehension), not ru'ya (vision). The two are distinct. This is the key insight.
Idrak implies encompassing, while ru'ya is merely sight.
4
Understand the second response: scope of hadith
The hadith only says Allah is not seen in this world, not that He cannot be seen in the Hereafter. The objection extends the hadith beyond its scope.
Nasafi challenges the assumption with 'لم قلتم' (why do you say?).
5
Understand the third response: direction is not implied
Nasafi distinguishes: if the seen object is in a direction, then seeing implies direction; but if it is not, then seeing does not require direction. Since Allah is not in a direction, ru'ya is possible without jiha.
This argument is similar to the analogy with knowledge ('كما قلنا في العلم').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إنسيا ) [مريم: ٢٦] ومع هذا لا يقتضي التأييد، وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿ لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَرُ ﴾ قلنا: النصُّ يقتضي انتفاء الإدراك، ولكن لا يقتضي انتفاء الرؤية. وأما حديث عائشة رضى الله عنها، قلنا: النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أخبر أنه لا يُري في الدنيا، ولكن لم قلتم بأنه لا يُرى في الآخرة؟ وأما قوله: لو قلنا يُرى يؤدي إلى إثبات الجهة. قلنا : متى ؟ إذا كان المرئي في الجهة أم إذا لم يكن. الأول: مسلَّم. والثاني: ممنوع، ولكن المرئي ههنا ليس في الجهة فلا يلزم من ضرورة انتفاء الإدراك انتفاء الرؤية وصار هذا كما قلنا في العلم.
And with this, it does not necessitate support. As for His saying, exalted is He: 'No vision can grasp Him' – we say: the text necessitates the negation of comprehension (idrak), but it does not necessitate the negation of seeing (ru'ya). As for the hadith of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her – we say: the Prophet, peace be upon him, informed that He is not seen in this world, but why do you say that He is not seen in the Hereafter? As for his saying: 'If we say He is seen, it leads to establishing direction (jiha)' – we say: when? If the seen object is in a direction or if it is not. The first is conceded; the second is denied. But the seen object here is not in a direction, so it does not follow from the necessity of negating comprehension the negation of seeing. And this is as we said regarding knowledge.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a response to three objections against the Sunni position that Allah will be seen in the Hereafter. First, the objector cites the verse 'No vision can grasp Him.' Nasafi responds that the verse negates comprehension (idrak), not vision (ru'ya) – the two are distinct. Second, the objector cites the hadith that the Prophet said no one can see Allah in this world. Nasafi points out that the hadith only denies seeing in the dunya, not in the akhira. Third, the objector argues that seeing implies direction. Nasafi distinguishes: if the seen object is in a direction, then direction is implied, but if it is not, then seeing does not require direction. Since Allah is not in a direction, seeing Him does not entail a direction for Him. Thus, none of the objections refute the possibility of ru'ya in the Hereafter.

Key Terms
رؤية (ru'ya)
إدراك (idrak)
جهة (jiha)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the verse 'No vision can grasp Him' (6:103) negates any form of seeing Allah, including in the Hereafter.
Correction: Nasafi clarifies that the verse negates idrak (comprehensive perception), not ru'ya (vision). The two are distinct, so the verse does not rule out ru'ya.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why does the verse 'No vision can grasp Him' not negate seeing Allah in the Hereafter?
A) Because the verse only refers to this world.
B) Because idrak (comprehension) is not the same as ru'ya (seeing).
C) Because the verse is abrogated.
D) Because seeing Allah is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The verse 'No vision can grasp Him' negates comprehension, not vision, and the other objections are similarly addressed by careful distinctions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'No vision can grasp Him,' did you ever stop to ask whether 'grasp' means the same as 'see'? How does this lesson challenge you to be more precise with Allah's words instead of assuming a superficial meaning?
?
If seeing Allah is the greatest reward of the Hereafter, why do you not find yourself yearning for it every day? What temporary delights have replaced that longing in your heart?
?
Nasafi clearly distinguishes between what is negated in this world and what is promised in the next. In your own life, do you confuse Allah's actions in different contexts and then accuse Him of inconsistency? What one assumption will you abandon today based on this lesson?

God Does Not Create Attributes in His Essence
Nasafi argues against God having created attributes in His essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why, according to Nasafi, God cannot have created attributes like blackness or redness within His essence.

Core Idea
God's essence cannot be a locus for created attributes.

Nasafi presents a concise argument affirming divine transcendence. He argues that God does not create qualities like blackness in Himself, because that would make His essence a place for temporal events, thereby resembling creatures. This is negated by the Qur'anic verse 'There is nothing like unto Him.' Let's examine this reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the key terms: صفة, ذات, محل للحوادث, شبيه.
The passage starts with 'به' which may be a continuation from a previous topic; focus on the core argument.
2
Identify the key claim and consequence
The author denies any possibility of God creating qualities like blackness in His essence. The consequence would be that His essence becomes a locus for temporal events, making it similar to created beings.
3
Understand the proof from the Qur'an
The verse 'There is nothing like unto Him' (42:11) is used to negate any resemblance. Reflect on how this verse supports the argument.
The verse is a cornerstone of Islamic tawhid.
4
Reflect on the importance for tawhid
Consider why this argument is crucial for preserving God's transcendence and uniqueness. How does it refute anthropomorphism?
This lesson reinforces the principle that God is not subject to temporal changes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
به صفةُ السواد والحُمْرة، ولا وجة إلى أن خَلَقَه في ذاته؛ لأنه حينئذ تكون ذاته محلاً للحوادث، فيكون ذاته شبيها بذوات المخلوقين ومثلهم، وإنه منفي بقوله تعالى: لَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ [الشورى: ١١].
With the quality of blackness and redness, and there is no possibility that He created it in His essence; because then His essence would be a locus for temporal events, so His essence would be similar to the essences of created beings and like them, and that is negated by His statement: 'There is nothing like unto Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing.'
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a concise argument about divine transcendence. The author asserts that God does not possess created qualities like blackness or redness in His essence, nor did He create them in Himself, because that would make His essence a substrate for temporal events, thereby likening Him to created beings. This is negated by the Quranic verse 'There is nothing like unto Him' (42:11). The reasoning follows the kalam principle that God's essence cannot be a locus for accidents.

Correction: This passage clarifies that such a belief would imply God's essence is a locus for temporal events, making Him resemble creatures, which is explicitly negated by the Qur'anic verse.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
God's essence is not a locus for temporal events, preserving His uniqueness as stated in Quran 42:11.

?

Attributing Effects to Means is Disbelief
Nasafi states that attributing the cure to means is kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that while means (asbab) are causes, the true agent of all effects is Allah alone, and attributing effects directly to means constitutes kufr.

Core Idea
Means are causes; Allah is the sole agent. Attributing effects to means is shirk.

Imam Nasafi presents a foundational principle of tawhid in causation: while means like medicine, work, and clothing are causes, the actual effect comes from Allah. This lesson clarifies that seeing (attributing) the effect to the means is disbelief, as it implies a partner with Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the full Arabic statement by Nasafi and its literal translation. Notice the repeating pattern: 'cause from Allah, but seeing the effect from the cause is kufr.'
The phrase 'رؤية الشفاء من الدواء' means 'seeing (attributing) the cure from the medicine'.
2
Understand the key distinction: cause vs. agent
Nasafi affirms that means are causes (sabab), but the ultimate agent (fa'il) is Allah. The error is to attribute the effect directly to the means, as if the means act independently.
This does not deny causality; it affirms secondary causation subject to Allah's power.
3
Identify the three examples
Find the three examples: 1) cure from medicine/doctor, 2) provision from earning, 3) repelling heat/cold from clothes. Note how each follows the same structure.
These are everyday examples to ground the theological principle.
4
Reflect on the implication for tawhid
Why is this kufr? Because it gives the means a share in Allah's exclusive power of creation and causation. It violates tawhid al-af'al (oneness of actions).
This guard against shirk in daily attitudes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطلب في رؤية الشفاء من الدواء أو من الطبيب. وعندنا الدواء سبب الشفاء من الله تعالى، ورؤية الشفاء من الدواء أو من الطبيب كفر، بل الشفاء من الله تعالى، هذا لأنه اتخذه شريكا مع الله تعالى في الشفاء. والكسب سبب والرزق من الله تعالى، ورؤية الرزق من الكسب كفر، وليس الثياب سبب دفع الحر والبرد، ودافع الحر والبرد هو الله سبحانه وتعالى، ورؤية دفع الحر والبرد من الثياب كفر.
Section on seeing the cure from the remedy or from the physician. And with us, the remedy is a cause of cure from Allah, and seeing the cure from the remedy or from the physician is disbelief; rather, the cure is from Allah. This is because he has taken it as a partner with Allah in curing. And earning is a cause, and provision is from Allah, and seeing provision from earning is disbelief. And clothes are not a cause for repelling heat and cold, and the repeller of heat and cold is Allah, and seeing the repelling of heat and cold from clothes is disbelief.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement on tawhid in causation. It defines the proper attribution of effects. Nasafi states that while means like medicine, earning, and clothing are causes (sabab), the ultimate effect comes from Allah alone. Attributing the effect directly to the means (ru'ya, seeing) is kufr because it implies shirk in Allah's sole power. He uses three examples: healing, provision, and protection from weather. The key is that the means are only instrumental; the true agent is Allah.

Key Terms
الشّفاء
الدواء
الكسب
الثياب
السبب
الشريك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Islamic theology denies all causality, but it affirms causes as secondary while the true agent is Allah. The warning is against attributing absolute effectiveness to causes.
Correction: Nasafi affirms means as causes (sabab) but stresses that the effect is directly from Allah. Attributing the effect to the means is kufr, not the use of means.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, what is the ruling on one who sees (attributes) the cure to the medicine or doctor?
A) It is permissible
B) It is a minor sin
C) It is kufr
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
Attributing effects directly to means is kufr because it implies a partner with Allah in causation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your cure comes from Allah alone, or do you, in your heart, put your trust in medicine and doctors as the actual givers of health? What can you do today to shift that reliance?
?
When you receive your salary or find a new job, do you attribute it to your own effort, or do you see it as provision from Allah? How can you remind yourself of this daily?
?
When you put on clothes to protect yourself from heat or cold, who do you think is actually repelling the heat? How does this passage challenge your habitual thinking, and what will you change?

Refutation of the Mafrughiyya: Creation Is Ongoing
Nasafi refutes the Mafrughiyya and defends the Sunni view of ongoing creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni refutation of the Mafrughiyya sect's claim that all creation is already finished, and why divine decree (qadr) is not identical to creation (khalq).

Core Idea
God decrees all things but creates them in their proper times.

The Mafrughiyya sect claimed that God has already created everything, even future fruits, citing a Quranic verse. The Sunni response distinguishes between God's decree and His actual creation, supported by multiple proofs from revelation and reason. This passage presents the central Sunni argument and addresses key objections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the structure: false claim, Sunni position, proofs, objections.
The passage is a complete refutation unit.
2
Identify the false claim and its proof
Find what the Mafrughiyya say and which verse they use. Understand their reasoning.
They believe everything is already created, citing Quran 2:29.
3
Understand the Sunni position and key evidence
Contrast with Sunni view: God decreed but creates in time. Note the evidence from Quran 55:29, hadith, and Ali's narration.
4
Examine additional proofs
Look at the rational proof from the Day of Resurrection not yet created, and the Pen and Tablet proof.
These show that things are decreed but not yet created.
5
Reflect on the objections and answers
See the two questions about the Pen and the wisdom of writing, and how they are answered.
The answers reinforce God's power and knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الرد على المفروغية القائلين إن الله خلق كل الأشياء ولم يبق شيء لم يخلقه. قال بعض أهل الباطل : إن الله تعالى خلق الأشياء كلها ولم يبق شيء غير مخلوق حتى يخلقه الآن، وكل ما كان مخلوقاً فرغ منها، حتى إن الثمار في الأشجار كلها، إلا أنها غير ظاهرة ونحن لا نراها وهي في الحقيقة مخلوقة. واحتجوا بقوله تعالى : ﴿هُوَ الَّذِي خَلَقَ لَكُم مَّا فِي الْأَرْضِ جَمِيعًا﴾ [البقرة: ٢٩]. وقال أهل السنة والجماعة : إن الله تعالى قدر ما هو كائن إلى يوم القيامة، ولم يخلقها حين قدرها، وإنما يخلقها بعد ذلك في كل وقت وأوان، خلق ما مضى وفي المستقبل يخلقها. يدل عليه قوله تعالى : ﴿كُلَّ يَوْمٍ هُوَ فِي شَأْنٍ﴾ [الرحمن: ٢٩] قال عليه السلام: «شأنه أن يحيي ويميت ويُعزّ ويُذل». وعن علي رضي الله عنه : أنه سُئل عن قوله تعالى: ﴿كُلَّ يَوْمٍ هُوَ فِي شَأْنٍ﴾ فقال: «شأنه أن يسوق النطفة من أصلاب الآباء إلى أرحام الأمهات، ثم يصور صورة ثم يُخرج من بطن الأم إلي الدنيا، ثم يميته، ثم يحييه يوم القيامة». يدل عليه أن الله تعالى قدر يوم القيامة وليس بمخلوق؛ ولأنه لو كان مخلوقاً لكنا نحن في القيامة وليس كذلك. ويدل عليه : أن الله تعالى خلق القلم ، وقال : اكتب ما هو كائن إلى يوم القيامة. فإن قيل : القلم هل فيه حياة؟ قلنا ليس فيه حياة، لكنه جمادٌ يستنطقه الله كما يستنطق الأحياء. فإن قيل: أيش الحكمة في أنَّ الله تعالى أمر القلم بأن يكتب على اللوح المحفوظ ما هو كائن إلى يوم القيامة وهو عالم؟ قلنا : لكي يُعلم أن الله تعالى يعلم الغيب ولا يعلم الغيب إلا الله.
Chapter on the refutation of the Mafrughiyya (those who say creation is finished) who say that God created all things and nothing remains that He did not create. Some of the people of falsehood said: God Almighty created all things, and nothing remains uncreated for Him to create now, and everything that was created He has finished from it, such that fruits on trees are all (created), except that they are not apparent and we do not see them, but in reality they are created. And they argued by His statement, the Exalted: 'He it is Who created for you all that is on the earth' (Quran 2:29). And Ahl al-Sunna wal-Jama'a said: God Almighty decreed what will happen until the Day of Resurrection, and He did not create them when He decreed them; rather He creates them after that in every time and season—He created what has passed, and in the future He creates them. Evidence for that is His statement, the Exalted: 'Every day He is upon some matter' (Quran 55:29). The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'His matter is that He gives life and causes death, and grants honor and humiliation.' And from Ali (may God be pleased with him): That he was asked about the statement of God, the Exalted: 'Every day He is upon some matter,' and he said: 'His matter is that He drives the sperm-drop from the loins of fathers to the wombs of mothers, then forms a form, then brings it out from the womb to the world, then causes it to die, then resurrects it on the Day of Resurrection.' Further evidence for that is that God Almighty decreed the Day of Resurrection and it is not created; because if it were created, we would be in the Resurrection, and that is not the case. And evidence for that also: that God Almighty created the Pen and said: Write what will be until the Day of Resurrection. If it is said: Does the Pen have life? We say: It has no life, but it is an inanimate object that God causes to speak just as He causes living beings to speak. If it is said: What is the wisdom in that God Almighty commanded the Pen to write on the Preserved Tablet what will happen until the Day of Resurrection while He is All-Knowing? We say: So that it be known that God Almighty knows the unseen, and none knows the unseen except God.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a group called the Mafrughiyya, who believe that God has already created everything in the past, including future fruits, even if they are not yet visible. They cite Quran 2:29 as evidence. The Sunni response is that God decreed (qaddara) all things but does not create them all at once; rather, He creates them in their proper times. They support this with Quran 55:29 ('Every day He is upon some matter') and a hadith explaining that matter includes giving life and death, honor and humiliation. The narration from Ali further clarifies that God's daily 'matter' includes the entire process of human generation and resurrection. The author then gives two additional proofs: (1) If the Day of Judgment were already created, we would be in it now; (2) God created the Pen and commanded it to write what will be until the Day of Judgment, implying that those things are not yet created but will be. Two objections are raised and answered: first, whether the Pen has life—it does not, but God makes it speak as He makes living things speak; second, why God would command the Pen to write if He already knows—the wisdom is to teach creation that God alone knows the unseen.

Key Terms
المفروغية
قدر
خلق
القلم
اللوح المحفوظ
يوم القيامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's decree (qadr) is the same as creation (khalq) – that everything decreed is already created.
Correction: The Sunni position distinguishes decree from creation: God decrees all things but creates them in their appointed times, as proven by the ongoing daily matters and the Day of Resurrection not yet created.

Checkpoint
On what basis do the Mafrughiyya claim that fruits on trees are already created?
A) They reason from God's omniscience.
B) They cite Quran 2:29 'He created for you all that is on the earth'.
C) They rely on a hadith about the Pen.
D) They deduce it from the Day of Judgment.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position affirms that God creates anew every day; His decree is not His creation, and future events exist only in knowledge until their appointed time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if God's creation is finished, expecting nothing new from Him, or do you wake each day anticipating His fresh 'shaan'—His new act of giving life, death, honor, or humiliation in your life? What would change if you truly believed He is creating new things every day?
?
When you look at your future—uncertain plans, fears, hopes—do you trust that God has already decreed it and will create it at the right time, or do you try to force it into existence yourself? How often do you pause to acknowledge that His timing is part of His creation?
?
The Pen wrote everything until the Day of Resurrection, but you do not see tomorrow yet. Does that make you anxious or peaceful? Are you content to let God be the only knower of the unseen, or do you secretly wish you had that knowledge to control your life?

Did the Prophet See His Lord? (Spiritual, Not Physical)
Nasafi addresses whether the Prophet saw Allah during the Mi'raj, citing hadith and Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that the Prophet saw Allah with his heart, not his physical eyes, during the Mi'raj, and the evidence for this.

Core Idea
The Prophet saw Allah spiritually, not physically.

The question of whether the Prophet ﷺ saw Allah during the Mi'raj has been a point of discussion. In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents the Sunni consensus based on the Prophet's own words and the Qur'an. The distinction between seeing with the heart and seeing with the eye is crucial for maintaining divine transcendence while affirming the Prophet's special honor. Let's examine the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Understand the central question being addressed.
Notice the two key pieces of evidence: a hadith and a Qur'anic verse.
2
Identify the Prophet's response
The Prophet said: 'I saw with my heart and did not see with my eye.' Reflect on the phrase 'سبحان الله' that precedes it.
This indicates Allah's transcendence and the impossibility of physical vision.
3
Consider the supporting report from 'A'isha
The report from 'A'isha confirms that the Prophet gave the same answer when asked about the vision.
This shows consistency in the Prophet's teaching.
4
Examine the Qur'anic verse
Verse 53:11 attributes vision to the heart, not the eye. This reinforces the distinction between spiritual and physical seeing.
The verse is from Surah al-Najm, which describes the Mi'raj.
5
Reflect on the theological significance
Why is it important that the vision was spiritual? How does this preserve divine transcendence?
This connects to the broader principle of tanzih (declaring Allah free from physical limitations).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم سُئل النبيُّ عليه السلام هل رأي ربه ليلة المعراج أم لا؟ قيل: رآه بقلبه وما رآه بعينه، لما رُوي عن النبي عليه السلام، قيل له: هل رأيت ربك ليلة المعراج ؟ فقال: سبحان الله رأيت بفؤادي وما رأيت بعيني. وعن عائشة رضي الله عنها أنها سألت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الرؤية فأجاب مثل ذلك. قال الله تعالى: ﴿مَا كَذَبَ الْفُؤَادُ مَا رَأَى ﴾ [النجم: ١١] أضاف الرؤية إلى الفؤاد لا إلى العين.
Then the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked: Did he see his Lord on the night of the Mi'raj or not? It was said: He saw Him with his heart and did not see Him with his eye, according to what was reported from the Prophet (peace be upon him). It was said to him: Did you see your Lord on the night of the Mi'raj? He said: 'Glory be to God! I saw with my heart and did not see with my eye.' And it is reported from 'A'isha (may God be pleased with her) that she asked the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) about the vision (ru'ya) and he replied similarly. God Most High said: 'The heart did not lie about what it saw' [al-Najm:11]. He attributed the vision to the heart, not to the eye.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage tackles a controversial question: Did the Prophet see Allah (ru'ya) during the Mi'raj? The answer given by the Sunni tradition, based on the Prophet's own words, is that he saw Him with his heart (bi-qalbihi/fu'adihi), not with his physical eyes (bi-'aynihi). Two pieces of evidence are cited: a direct hadith in which the Prophet says 'رأيت بفؤادي وما رأيت بعيني' ('I saw with my heart and did not see with my eye'), and the report from 'A'isha that she asked the same question and received the same answer. Finally, the Qur'anic verse 'ما كذب الفؤاد ما رأى' (Surah al-Najm, 11) is quoted: here, the act of seeing (ru'ya) is attributed to the heart (fu'ad), not the eye, supporting the distinction. Thus the passage affirms a spiritual vision of Allah, not a physical one, preserving divine transcendence (tanzih) while acknowledging the Prophet's special honor.

Key Terms
رأى
رب
الرؤية
الفؤاد
العين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim the Prophet physically saw Allah with his eyes during the Mi'raj.
Correction: This passage clarifies that the Prophet himself said he saw with his heart, not his eyes, and the Qur'an attributes vision to the heart.

Checkpoint
How did the Prophet describe seeing his Lord?
A) He saw Him with his eyes.
B) He saw Him with his heart, not his eyes.
C) He did not see Him at all.
D) He saw Him in a dream.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet saw Allah spiritually with his heart during the Mi'raj, not with his physical eyes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet said, 'I saw with my heart.' When you seek Allah, do you look for Him in physical signs and miracles, or do you strive to see Him with your heart through sincerity and reflection? What would change if you prioritized inner vision over outer proof?
?
If you were to ask the Prophet today about seeing Allah, his answer would be the same: 'Glory be to God! I saw with my heart, not my eye.' Does that truth confront any reliance you have on worldly appearances to feel close to Allah? How can you train your heart to see Him in the unseen?
?
Allah attributes the vision to the heart in the Quran. Have you ever experienced a moment when your heart 'saw' something true about Allah that your eyes could not? That is the kind of vision the Prophet had. Do you live as if that is possible, or do you dismiss it as something only for prophets? What is holding you back from seeking that connection?

The Prophet's Vision: Heart, Not Eyes
The author clarifies that the Prophet saw Allah with his heart, not his eyes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's vision of Allah on the night of the Mi'raj was a vision of the heart, not the physical eyes, based on explicit prophetic and Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
The Prophet saw Allah with his heart, not his eyes.

This lesson addresses a central question about the Mi'raj: did the Prophet see Allah with his physical eyes? The Sunni position, grounded in the Prophet's own words and a Quranic verse, is that the vision was spiritual. We will examine the textual evidence and its implications for understanding divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the narrative unfold before you interpret.
Notice the sequence: question, answer, evidence.
2

The verse is Surah An-Najm, verse 11.
3

Reflect on why this distinction matters: it preserves Allah's transcendence by affirming that He cannot be seen with physical eyes in this world.
This is consistent with the Sunni creed that Allah is not seen in the world but will be seen in the Hereafter.
4
Reflect on the meaning of heart-vision
Consider what it means to see with the heart. This is a spiritual, inner perception that goes beyond physical sight.
The heart (fu'ad) is the seat of spiritual knowledge and faith.

The Throne and the Footstool: Literal or Metaphor?
Refutation of metaphorical interpretation of 'Arsh and Kursi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that the Throne and Footstool are real physical creations, and why the metaphorical interpretations of the Mu'tazila and Shi'a are rejected.

Core Idea
The Throne is not just dominion; it is a physical creation carried by angels.

In this lesson, we examine a key dispute in Islamic theology: the nature of Allah's Throne ('Arsh) and Footstool (Kursi). Are they merely metaphors for dominion and knowledge, as the Mu'tazila and Shi'a claim, or are they literal physical entities? The People of the Sunnah present clear evidence from the Quran and hadith to affirm their physical reality. Let's see how they argue.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: first the opposing view, then the Sunni response with evidence.
Pay attention to the Quranic verses quoted.
2
Identify the two positions
Find the Mu'tazila/Shi'a interpretation and the Sunni interpretation. What is the key difference?
The Mu'tazila say 'Arsh = mulk (dominion), Kursi = 'ilm (knowledge).
3
Examine the Sunni evidence
The Sunni side uses two main proofs: a Quranic verse about the Throne being carried, and a hadith about angels carrying it. Understand why these prove physicality.
Dominion cannot be carried, so the Throne must be a physical entity.
4
Note the details about the angels
The hadith describes the number of angels carrying the Throne (4 in this world, 8 on Judgment Day) and their faces. This reinforces the literal interpretation.
These details are not symbolic; they are real descriptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الكلام على العرش والكرسي. قالت المعتزلة والشيعة: العرش هو الملك والكرسي هو العلم. قال الله تعالى: وَسِعَ كُرْسِيُّهُ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٥] أي علمه. وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: لا يجوز أن يكون العرش هو الملك، لأن الله تعالى قال: ﴿وَيَحْمِلُ عَرْشَ رَبِّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ ثَمَانِيَةٌ ﴾ [الحاقة : ١٧] والملك لا يحتاج إلى الحمل. وكذلك رُوِيَ عن النبي أنه قال: «لما خلق الله تعالى العرش خلق ملائكة، فقال: احملوا عرشي، فلم يستطيعوا أن يحملوا، قال الله تعالى: لو خَلَقْتُ مثل عددِ الرَّمل وقطر الأمطار، فلم يستطيعوا أن يحملوا مالم يستغيثوا بي، فقالوا: اللهم أغثنا، فسمعوا الله تعالى ـ بلا كيف - قولوا: لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله العلي العظيم، فقالوا، فحملوا العرش واستوى على رؤوسهم. وهم أربعة في الدنيا، وثمانية في الآخرة، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَيَحْمِلُ عَرْشَ رَبِّكَ فَوْقَهُمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ ثَمَانِيَةٌ ﴾ [الحاقة: ١٨] والملائكة الأربعة الذين يحملون العرش لكل واحد منهم أربعة أوجه: وجه ثور، والآخر أسد، والآخر وجه نسر، والآخر وجه إنسان.
Chapter on discourse concerning the Throne and the Footstool. The Mu'tazila and the Shi'a said: The Throne is the dominion and the Footstool is knowledge. Allah Most High said: 'His Footstool extends over the heavens and the earth' [Al-Baqara 2:255] meaning His knowledge. And the People of the Sunnah and the Community said: It is not permissible that the Throne be the dominion, because Allah Most High said: 'And the Throne of your Lord will be carried above them on that Day by eight' [Al-Haqqa 69:17], and dominion does not need to be carried. Likewise, it is narrated from the Prophet ﷺ that he said: 'When Allah Most High created the Throne, He created angels and said: Carry My Throne. They could not carry it. Allah Most High said: If I created the like of the number of sand and the drops of rain, they could not carry it until they seek help from Me. So they said: O Allah, help us. Then they heard Allah Most High - without how - saying: Say: There is no power and no strength except with Allah, the Most High, the Magnificent. They said it, and they carried the Throne and it settled upon their heads. They are four in this world and eight in the Hereafter. Allah Most High said: 'And the Throne of your Lord will be carried above them on that Day by eight' [Al-Haqqa 69:18]. And the four angels who carry the Throne, each one of them has four faces: a face of an ox, another of a lion, another of an eagle, and another of a human.'
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the metaphorical interpretation of the Throne ('Arsh) and the Footstool (Kursi) by the Mu'tazila and Shi'a. The author begins by stating their position: that 'Arsh means dominion and Kursi means knowledge, citing the verse 'His Kursi extends over the heavens and the earth' as evidence that Kursi is knowledge. Then the author presents the position of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, which is that the Throne cannot be dominion because Allah says it will be carried by angels on the Day of Judgment, and dominion is an abstract concept that cannot be physically carried. The author then supports this with a hadith in which Allah commands angels to carry the Throne, they fail, and then they succeed after saying 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah'. This hadith emphasizes the physical reality of the Throne and the angels carrying it. The passage further describes the number of angels carrying the Throne: four in this world, eight on the Day of Judgment, each having four faces: an ox, a lion, an eagle, and a human. Thus, the Sunni position affirms the literal, physical existence of the Throne and Kursi as created entities, rejecting metaphorical interpretations.

الكرسي (al-Kursi)
الملك (al-mulk)
العلم (al-'ilm)
المعتزلة (al-Mu'tazila)
الشيعة (al-Shi'a)
أهل السنة والجماعة (Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Throne and Footstool are merely metaphors for God's dominion and knowledge.
Correction: According to Ahl al-Sunnah, they are real physical creations that will be carried by angels, as indicated by the Quran and hadith.

Checkpoint

B) Because dominion does not need to be carried, whereas the Throne is described as being carried.
C) Because the Mu'tazila said so, and they are always wrong.
D) Because the Footstool is knowledge, and the Throne is different.

Key Takeaway
The Throne and Footstool are real, physical creations, not mere metaphors for God's attributes.

Wisdom and Substance of the Throne
Nasafi reports two wisdoms and two views on the Throne's substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two wisdoms reported for the creation of the Throne and the differing views on its material substance.

Core Idea
The Throne serves as a qibla and mirror for angels, and its substance is debated.

In this passage, Nasafi transmits two explanations for why Allah created the Throne and reports the disagreement among scholars about what the Throne is made of. These details are not essential articles of faith but reflect the broader Islamic tradition's engagement with the unseen. The passage invites reflection on divine wisdom and the limits of human knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the translation. Notice the structure: first wisdoms, then substance.
The passage uses the phrase 'قال بعضهم' (some said) and 'واختلفوا' (they differed).
2
Identify the two wisdoms
Find the two wisdoms: the Throne as a direction for angelic supplication and as a mirror for angels to see the cosmos.
Both are transmitted, not confirmed by revelation.
3
Note the disagreement on the substance
Distinguish the two opinions: some say it is a bed of light, others say it is of red ruby. The author does not choose.
This shows the speculative nature of such topics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الحِكْمَةُ فِي خَلْقِ العرش فقال بعضهم: قبله دعاء الملائكة، ويرفعون أيديهم إلى العرش وقت الدعاء، وقيل: إنه مرآة الملائكة ينظرون إليه فيرون جميع ما كان في السموات والأرض. واختلفوا في العرش، قال بعضهم: سَرِيرٌ من نور، وقال بعضهم: لا، بل هو من ياقوتة حمراء.
As for the wisdom in the creation of the Throne, some said: It is a direction for the supplication of the angels, and they raise their hands to the Throne at the time of supplication. And it is said: It is a mirror for the angels; they look at it and see all that is in the heavens and the earth. And they differed concerning the Throne: Some said: It is a bed of light. And some said: No, rather it is of red ruby.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory report about the Throne. First, the author presents two wisdoms (hikma) for its creation: (1) It serves as a qibla (direction) for the angels' supplication — they raise their hands towards it when praying. (2) It functions as a mirror (mir'ah) for the angels, allowing them to see everything in the heavens and earth by looking at it. Second, the author notes a difference of opinion among scholars regarding the substance of the Throne: some say it is a couch (sarir) made of light (nur); others say it is made of a single red ruby (yaquta hamra'). The author does not adjudicate between these views but simply transmits them.

Key Terms
الحكمة
دعاء الملائكة
مرآة
سرير من نور
ياقوتة حمراء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The wisdoms reported are definitive, divinely revealed facts about the Throne.
Correction: These are transmitted opinions (some said, it is said) and not certain knowledge. They are speculative explanations.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what are the two reported wisdoms for the creation of the Throne?
A) As a throne for Allah and a place for angels to pray.
B) As a direction for angelic supplication and as a mirror for angels to see the cosmos.
C) As a source of light and a red ruby.
D) As a symbol of Allah's power and a repository of knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The wisdom of the Throne's creation is explained in two transmitted ways, and its substance remains a matter of scholarly disagreement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The angels raise their hands toward the Throne when they supplicate. When you make du'a, do you have a clear direction of focus that reminds you of Allah's majesty, or is your mind scattered? How can you cultivate a qibla for your heart?
?
The Throne serves as a mirror for the angels to see all creation. If you truly believed that every action of yours is observed by angels and known to Allah, would you change anything in your daily life? What specific habit would you start or stop today?
?
The scholars disagreed about the Throne's substance, yet they did not fight over it. Is there a matter of religious disagreement where you have been more attached to a particular view than to the humility of acknowledging that only Allah knows the Unseen? Will you release that attachment?

The Throne's Purpose and Substance
Nasafi reports wisdom for creating the Throne and differing opinions on its substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two transmitted explanations for the wisdom of creating the Throne and the differing opinions on its physical nature.

Core Idea
The Throne serves a purpose for the angels, yet its true nature remains a matter of scholarly debate.

This passage from Nasafi's work addresses a topic of theological curiosity: why did Allah create the Throne, and what is it made of? Nasafi reports two explanations for the wisdom behind the Throne's creation, and then notes a disagreement about its substance—whether it is light or red ruby. The passage does not resolve the debate but presents the views as transmitted.

Reflect on the transmission

Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage discusses two matters: first, the wisdom (al-hikma) in Allah's creation of the Throne, and second, the differing opinions on what the Throne actually is. The author presents two views on the wisdom: (1) that the angels pray facing the Throne and raise their hands toward it during supplication, and (2) that the Throne serves as a mirror for the angels, enabling them to see everything in the heavens and earth. Then he mentions the disagreement about the Throne's substance: some say it is a throne of light, others say it is made of red ruby. ?
The disagreement about the Throne's substance reminds us that even scholars differ on matters of the unseen. Does your faith rely on knowing the exact nature of things, or are you willing to submit to Allah's mystery? Practice trusting Allah's wisdom even when you don't have all the answers.

The Same Body at Resurrection
Imam Nasafi refutes the claim of a new body at resurrection and interprets Quranic 'change' as attribute change.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quranic verse about changing skins does not support the creation of a new body at resurrection, and how the change is one of attributes, not essence.

Core Idea
Resurrection is not a new body – it's the same body transformed.

Imam Nasafi addresses a claim that at resurrection, Allah creates an entirely new body for the soul, citing Quran 4:56 as evidence. He explains that the verse refers to changing attributes, not the essence, and supports his interpretation with Quran 14:48. This lesson clarifies the Islamic position on bodily resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Understand the heretical claim
Read the first part of the passage where the group asserts that a new body is created for the soul after death. Note their analogy of the body as a cloak.
2
Examine their evidence
Look at their proof from Quran 4:56 about replacing skins. Consider why they think this supports a new body.
3
Analyze the refutation
Read Imam Nasafi's response: the change is of attributes, not essence. He uses Quran 14:48 as a parallel.
4
Apply the principle
Understand that this hermeneutical rule applies to other verses: 'change' often means transformation, not replacement.
This protects the doctrine of bodily resurrection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصنف منهم قالوا: إذا مات الرجل وصار رميمًا يخلق الله تعالى له جسدا آخر تدخل فيه الروح، وقالوا بأن الجسد للروح كالجبة للبدن، واحتجوا بقوله تعالى: (كلما نَضِجَتْ جُلُودُهُم بَدَّلْنَهُمْ جُلُودًا غَيْرَهَا لِيَذُوقُوا الْعَذَابَ) [النساء : ٥٦].
قلنا: أراد به تبديل هيئاتها وصفاتها، لا تبديل عينها، يدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿ يَوْمَ تُبَدَّلُ الْأَرْضُ غَيْرَ الْأَرْضِ وَالسَّمَوَاتُ وَبَرَزُوا لِلَّهِ الْوَاحِدِ الْقَهَّارِ ) [إبراهيم: ٤٨] وأراد به تبديل صفتها لا تبديل عينها كذلك ههنا.
And a group of them said: When a man dies and becomes decayed bones, Allah Almighty creates for him another body into which the soul enters. And they said that the body is to the soul like the cloak is to the body. And they argued with His statement: (Every time their skins are roasted, We will replace them with other skins so that they may taste the punishment) [An-Nisa: 56]. We said: He intended by it the changing of their forms and attributes, not the changing of their essence. This is supported by His statement: (On the Day when the earth will be changed to another earth and the heavens, and they will appear before Allah, the One, the Subduer) [Ibrahim: 48] and He intended by it the changing of its attribute, not the changing of its essence. Likewise here.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage refutes a heretical claim about resurrection. A group (probably Rawafid again, but not specified) claims that when a man dies and decays, Allah creates an entirely new body for him, and the soul enters that new body. They compare the body to a cloak (jubbah) worn by the soul. They support this with Quran 4:56, where Allah says that the skins of the inhabitants of Hell are replaced whenever they are roasted, so that they continue to taste punishment. The author refutes this by explaining the meaning of 'replacement' in the verse. He says: Allah intended the changing of their forms and attributes (hay'atiha wa sifatiha), not the changing of their very essence ('ayniha). He then provides supporting evidence from Quran 14:48, where Allah says that the earth will be changed to another earth. The author notes that this change is of attributes, not of essence; the same earth is transformed, not annihilated and replaced. Likewise, the replacement of skins in Hell is a transformation of their physical qualities (e.g., from burnt to fresh) to enable perpetual suffering, not a new body for a different soul. The point is that at resurrection, it is the same body that is restored, not a completely new one.

Key Terms
رميم
تبديل
هيئة
صفة
عين
جبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Quran 4:56 supports the idea that Allah creates a brand new body for the soul at resurrection.
Correction: The verse refers to changing the attributes of the skin to enable continuous punishment, not creating a new substance. The same body is transformed.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, what does the Quranic phrase 'replace their skins' (بدّلناهم جلودا غيرها) mean?
A) It means creating entirely new bodies for the souls.
B) It means changing their qualities and attributes, not their essence.
C) It means the souls will get new bodies while the old ones remain.
D) It is a metaphor for spiritual suffering.

Key Takeaway
Resurrection restores the same body, transformed in attributes, not replaced with a new one.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your body is the same one that will be resurrected, how does that change the way you treat your body today? What one habit will you change starting today to honor that truth?
?
The heretics argued that the body is like a cloak for the soul. Do you live as if your body is disposable or as an integral part of your eternal identity? What needs to change in your daily actions to reflect that your body has eternal significance?
?
The change on the Day of Judgment is a transformation of attributes, not essence. What attributes in your character need to be transformed now so that your essence is prepared for that day? What concrete step will you take this week to begin that change?

Module 5 · Lesson 73

Divine Transcendence
beginner
5 min
Refuting the Astrologers' Claim of Celestial Management
Nasafi refutes the astrological claim that celestial bodies manage affairs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunnah rejects the astrological claim that celestial bodies independently manage earthly affairs, and why this is a matter of tawheed.

Core Idea
Only Allah manages creation; stars and planets are subjugated.

This lesson presents a fundamental dispute: do celestial bodies have independent influence over human affairs, or are they merely subjugated creations under Allah's command? The astrologers' claim seems plausible to some, but it undermines tawheed. Here, Imam Nasafi lays out the Sunni position with clear scriptural evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the two opposing views presented.
Notice the clear contrast between 'mudabbirat' and 'musakhkharat'.
2
Identify the astrologers' position
What do astrologers claim about the zodiac and planets? They say these bodies manage affairs and that knowledge of them brings benefit and protection.
Also note their belief that one can know the time of death.
3
Identify the Sunni position
Ahl al-Sunnah respond that all celestial bodies are subjugated (musakhkharat) and have no management. Only Allah is the Manager.
The Quranic verse is the proof.
4
Reflect on the theological principle
Why is this refutation important? It upholds tawheed al-rububiyyah—Allah alone is the Creator and Controller of all affairs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل [ في الرد على أهل النجوم]
قال أهل النجوم: أمور أهل الأرض متعلة بالبروج الاثني عشر وبالنجوم السبعة [وهي زحل، والمشترى ،والمريخ، والزهرة، والشمس، وعطارد، والقمر ] (١). وقالوا بأن هذه البروج والنجوم مدبرات لأهل الأرض، فكل من علم [النجوم ](٢) يعرف صلاح نفسه ويمكنه أن يميل إلى ما هو خير له، ويحترز عما هو شر له، ويعلم متى يموت
وقال أهل السنة والجماعة: هذه البروج والنجوم والشمس والقمر وجميع النيرات مسخرات ليس لها من التدبير شيء، ومدبر الأمور (۳) هو الله تعالى كما قال الله تعالى: وَالشَّمْسَ وَالْقَمَرَ وَالنُّجُومُ مُسَخَّرَاتُ بأمروه ﴾ [النحل: ١٢]. بِأَمْرِهِ
Chapter [On Refutation of the Astrologers]
The astrologers said: The affairs of the people of earth are connected to the twelve zodiac signs and the seven planets [which are Saturn, Jupiter, Mars, Venus, the Sun, Mercury, and the Moon] (1). And they said that these zodiac signs and planets are managers for the people of earth, so whoever knows [astrology] (2) knows his own welfare, and can incline toward what is good for him, and beware of what is evil for him, and knows when he will die.
And Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah said: These zodiac signs, planets, sun, moon, and all luminaries are subjugated; they have nothing of management, and the Manager of affairs (3) is Allah Almighty, as Allah Almighty said: 'And the sun, the moon, and the stars are subjugated by His command' (an-Nahl 16:12). By His command.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of astrology (tanjim). It begins by presenting the astrologers' claim: that the affairs of people on earth are linked to the twelve zodiac signs and seven planets, which they consider to be active managers (mudabbirat). Astrologers believed that knowledge of these celestial bodies allowed one to determine personal welfare, avoid harm, and learn the time of death. In response, Ahl al-Sunnah assert that all these celestial bodies—zodiac signs, planets, sun, moon, and other luminaries—are subjugated (musakhkharat), meaning they have no independent ability to manage or cause events. The sole Manager (mudabbir) is Allah, and they cite Quran 16:12, which states they are 'subjugated by His command.' This establishes tawhid al-rububiyyah, affirming that all creation is under Allah's control and no part of creation has independent agency.

Key Terms
أهل النجوم
البروج
النيرات
مسخرات
مدبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Astrology is harmless fortune-telling that does not affect one's faith.
Correction: Astrology attributes independent management to created beings, which contradicts tawheed al-rububiyyah—the belief that only Allah controls all affairs.

Checkpoint
What is the key argument of Ahl al-Sunnah against the astrologers?
A) The celestial bodies are too far away to affect earth.
B) The celestial bodies are subjugated and have no management; only Allah manages.
C) Astrology is a valid science but should not be used for predictions.
D) The astrologers are mistaken about the number of planets.

Key Takeaway
Celestial bodies have no independent management; all affairs are under Allah's sole control, as affirmed by the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face an uncertain future, do you unconsciously consult horoscopes or patterns in the stars? What does that reveal about whom you truly trust as the Manager of your life?
?
Is there any created thing—a person, a system, or a natural force—that you have been subconsciously attributing influence or control to, apart from Allah? How can you uproot that from your heart today?
?
This passage declares that the sun, moon, and stars have no management at all. If even these mighty creations are powerless, then what excuse is there for relying on anything other than Allah? Are you willing to repent and redirect your trust entirely to Him?
